قال واضع هذا الكتاب لمّا أكملت لكم يا بنىّ هذا الكتاب الذى هو جزء العلم في الطب بكماله وبلغت الغاية فيه من وضوحه وبيانه رأيت أن أكمله لكم بهذه المقالة التى هى جزء العمل باليد.
لأنّ العمل باليد محسن في بلادنا وفي زماننا معدوم البتة حتى كاد أن يدرس علمه وينقطع أثره. وإنّما بقى منه رسوم يسيرة في كتب الأوائل قد صحّفته الأيدي وواقعه الخطأ والتشويش حتى استغلقت معانيه وبعدها فائدة.
فرأيت أن أحييه وأؤلف فيه هذه المقالة على طريق الشرح والبيان والاختصار وأن آتى بصور حدائد الكى وسائر آلات العمل إذ هو من زيادة البيان ومن كيد ما يحتاج إليه.
والسبب الذي لا يوجد صانع محسن بيده في زماننا هذا لأنه صناعة الطب طيبة وينبغي لصاحبه أن يرتاض قبل ذلك في علم التشريح الذي وصفه جالينوس. حتّى يقف على منافع الأعضاء وهيآتها ومزاجاتها واتّصالها وانفصالها ومعرفة العظام والأعصاب والعضلات وعددها ومخارجها والعروق ينبض والسواكن ومواضع مخرجاتها.
ولذلك قال ابقرات إنّ الأطبّاء بالاسم كثير وبالفعل قليل ولا سيّما في صناعة اليد، وقد ذكرنا نحن من ذلك طرفا في المدخل من هذا الكتاب.
Because one who is not knowledgeable about what we have mentioned concerning anatomy may still fall into error that could kill people, as I have often witnessed with those who conceived in this science and claimed expertise without knowledge or understanding.
And I have seen a physician, ignorant of anatomy, who incised an abscess in a woman's neck and severed some of the jugular veins, causing her to bleed to death before him.
And I have seen another physician who, in extracting a stone from a man who had been stabbed in the kidney, and the stone was large, acted rashly and extracted it with a piece of bladder tissue. And the man died within about three days, and I had been summoned to extract it; I saw from the size of the stone and the condition of the patient what I had anticipated.
And I have seen another physician who earned his living as a quack among some of the governors in our city.
And I have seen a child of mine who had a fracture in his leg near the ankle, along with a wound. The physician, acting out of ignorance, tightened the bandages and splints around the fracture and wound very tightly, leaving no room for the wound to breathe.
Then he released him to his desires, left him for days, and ordered him not to loosen the bandage until his leg and foot swelled, almost leading to his death.
And I was summoned to him, so I hastened to release the bandage, and he found relief and was able to move from his pain. However, the corruption had become severe in the limb, and I could not reverse it.
腐败继续在组织中蔓延直至其死亡。
And I saw a physician delay in incising a malignant tumor until its condition worsened, the fate of his companion becoming severe. This is because if the cancer is pure black bile, it should never be treated with iron at all.
Except in a case where the entire organ can be removed.
And for this reason, my son, you must know that work by hand is divided into two parts: work that is accompanied by safety, and work that is often accompanied by harm in most cases.
And I have warned of every place in this book where the work involves risk and fear, so you must beware of it and reject it.
Lest the ignorant find a way to criticize and attack, be firm and cautious with yourselves and gentle but steadfast in treating your patients.
And use the best path leading to safety and the noble outcome, and avoid dangerous and difficult diseases.
And keep yourselves pure from what you fear may cast doubt upon your faith and in this world. It will be more lasting for your glory and higher in this world and the hereafter according to your station.
For Galen has said in some of his instructions: "Do not treat a bad disease and become a bad physician.
And this article has been divided into three parts.
The First Chapter.
In branding with fire and branding with sharp medicine, it is arranged from head to foot, and the instruments of branding, iron tools for branding, and all that is needed for handwork.
The Second Chapter.
In incision and reduction, extraction of foreign bodies and arrows, cupping and surgery, it is arranged from head to foot, and the instruments are illustrated.
The Third Chapter.
In resettings and divorces, and the treatment of dislocations, it is arranged from head to foot, and the instruments are illustrated.
The First Chapter.
In branding.
And before we mention its use, it is necessary to discuss its benefits and drawbacks, and in which conditions it should be used.
I say that the discussion of the benefits and drawbacks of branding is a long one, requiring a precise science and a hidden secret. Many wise men have spoken about it.
And they differed in their opinions. I have summarized only a little of their discussion to avoid making it too lengthy.
I say that branding is beneficial in general for all bad humors, whether present with a substance or without a substance, except for two humors: the hot humor without a substance and the dry humor without a substance.
If the dry temperament with matter differs, some have said that colocynth is beneficial in it and others contrary to that say that colocynth does not suit a disease arising from heat and dryness because the nature of fire is heat and dryness.
And it is impossible to cure a hot and dry disease with a hot and dry remedy, and those who say contrary to that have said that colocynth by the fire may be beneficial for a hot and dry disease that occurs in human bodies. Because if you add the humidity of the human body to the temperament of fire, you will make the human body cold.
And I say as he says because experience has shown me this many times, but it should not be imagined without great familiarity and extensive training in the use of colocynth. And he stopped to consider the differences in temperaments of people and the conditions of diseases within themselves, as well as their causes, symptoms, and duration.
And as for the other temperaments, you have no fear from them, and particularly not from cold and humid diseases, which all physicians agree on, and there is no disagreement about the benefit of colocynth in such cases.
And know, my sons, that the colocynth by fire is preferable to colocynth by a burning drug. For fire is an elementary substance whose effect does not extend beyond the organ it burns, and it harms another connected organ only slightly.
And colocynth by a burning drug may extend its effect to organs beyond, and it might cause a disease in another organ that is difficult to cure. And though fire, due to its dignity and the excellence of its nature, does not do this except if it is excessive.
And this became clear to us through experience due to the length of service and attention to the craft and standing firm on the realities of the matter.
And for this reason, I have abstained from lengthy speech. Were it not that it would not be fitting for my book, I would have revealed to you secretly the nature of fire and its actions on bodies, and its cure for diseases with a philosophical and demonstrative discourse that would penetrate your understanding.
And know, O my sons, that they have differed on the time in which branding is suitable and they have made the best time the time of spring.
And I say that branding is suitable at all times, for the harm caused by time itself is absorbed by the benefit brought about by branding. And especially if the branding is for a strong, urgent pain that cannot tolerate delay, as it fears that greater harm may follow than the usual damage caused by time.
And let it not occur to your mind, O my sons, what the common people and ignorant physicians might imagine—that branding which cures a certain illness will never return. You should not consider it harmful.
And both these matters are not considered so, because branding is like a medicine that alters the temperament and dries up the humors which are the cause of pain.
Except that branding is preferred to medicine because of the speed of its success, the strength of its effect, and the intensity of its power.
It may return at times of the year according to the temperament of the patient and the strength and potency of his disease, and what is present in his body from the coming together of superfluities in him and his neglect in acquiring them from food and such causes.
Ought to be that the disease in which cupping is used is a mild one and in an organ with little superfluity and humidity. Like cupping for toothache and the like, it may not return that pain, and this is in the lesser degree.
And as for the general belief that cupping is the end of medicine, this is a correct saying not as they intend it, because they believe that there is no remedy that benefits with a drug or otherwise after the application of cupping. The matter is contrary to this.
And the meaning that cupping is the end of medicine is that whenever we use various remedies for a disease and they do not work, then when we apply cupping, it works. From here, we conclude that cupping is the end of medicine. Not according to the meaning that the general public and many physicians who are ignorant of medicine have adopted.
And I have mentioned earlier that cupping with gold is better than cupping with iron, and they said this because of the moderation of gold and its noble nature. They also said that it does not congeal at the site of the cupping, though this is not absolutely true.
Because I have tried this and found that it only does so in some parts of the body and not others. Cupping with gold is better and preferable to iron, as they said; though if you heat the iron poker in the fire until it reaches the desired temperature for the redness of the gold, you may not be able to determine when to remove it.
Because it quickly reaches the coldness and if you increase upon it in fever it dissolves in fire and becomes molten. Therefore, it causes the maker to be occupied. For this reason, cautery with iron has become quicker and closer to correctness for the work, God willing.
I have arranged this chapter on cautery into sections organized from the head to the feet, making it easier for the student to understand what is required of him, God willing.
The First Section.
Cauterization of the Head with One Cautery.
This cautery is beneficial for the excess of dampness and cold in the brain, which are the causes of headaches, frequent nasal discharges from the head to the sides of the eyes and ears, excessive sleepiness, toothache, and throat pain. In short, for any disease caused by coldness such as paralysis, epilepsy, and fainting, and similar ailments.
The procedure for this cautery is to order the patient first to vomit with a mild and purgative medicine three or four days, depending on the strength of the patient, their age, and their usual condition.
Then order him to shave his head with scissors. Place him in front of you on a stool, with his hands resting on his chest.
Then place the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his eyes. Wherever your middle finger ends, mark that spot with a pen.
Then heat the oil lamp iron, which is its shape shown here.
An opened space in the bone equal to the size of a barleycorn or a peas kernel, raise your hand, otherwise replace it with the same tongs or another if it has cooled. Until you see from the bone what you were told. Then take a bit of salt, dissolve it in water, soak a cotton in it, put it on the place, and leave it for three days.
Then apply a cotton soaked in oil and leave it there until the inflammation subsides. Then treat it with the quadruple ointment until it heals, God willing.
And they said that the wound is better and more beneficial the longer it remains open to drain pus.
And some mentioned that the skin should be cauterized down to the bone, and the hot iron should be held until part of the thickness of the bone is burned. Then, remove what was burned from the bone, and proceed with treatment.
And others said that one should cauterize extensively until it affects the bone strongly, causing a piece of it to fall off like a carat or a small seed. They claimed that this releases vapors from that area and keeps the wound open for a long time.
Then treat until it heals. I do not see these two types of cauterization at all except in some people, and leaving it alone is better with safety. If it does heal, the head will expand when its natural connection is separated as we have seen in other organs.
And especially if the patient's head is naturally weak. The first type of cauterization is preferable and better for me; use it if you choose to do so, God willing.
The Second Chapter.
In the Correction of the Head Also.
If a chronic pain occurs in the head and continues to affect the patient, and if various treatments such as massage, fomentations, inhalations, enemas, and dressings have been used without any benefit, especially if the same cauterization that we described has been applied and no relief is obtained, then examine. If the head of the patient is strong by nature and not weak, and he finds extreme coldness, then apply another cauterization slightly above the previous one. Then apply a cauterization to each temple of his head until the thick skin is gone and the amount of bone that we described becomes visible. And apply a cauterization at the back of his head in the place known as the axe, but be gentle with your hand in this; do not reveal the bone, for the patient finds great pain from it unlike the pain from all other cauterizations of the head. I will describe this cauterization in its proper place.
And the cauterizing iron used for the horns of the head and its back should be softer than that used for the middle of the head. This is its shape.
The Third Chapter.
In the Correction of the Acute Hemicrania.
If a sharp pain occurs in the side of the head with headache, and the pain extends to the eye, cause the patient to vomit using remedies that cleanse the head, and apply all the treatment I mentioned in the divisions of diseases. If this is ineffective, cauterize it in two ways. Either cauterization with the sharp burning drug or with iron.
Either cauterization with the burning drug is as follows: Take one clove of garlic, peel it, and cut its ends from both sides. Then, use a broad forceps to make an incision at the site of pain in the cheek until there is a space under the skin large enough for the clove.
It is inserted under the skin until it disappears, then it is tightly tied with ligatures. It is left for about fifteen hours, then loosened and the garlic is removed. The wound is left open for two or three days, then treated further.
Apply it with a cotton pad soaked in oil until the area becomes suppurated. Then treat it with ointment until it heals, if Allah wills. If you prefer, you can use some of the burning drugs mentioned in the eighteenth article on burning drugs.
And cauterization with iron is as follows: Heat the tongs, which is shown in this image:
And it is called the nail tongs because its head resembles a nail, with some curvature and a small peg in the middle.
Then place it on the site of pain, hold your hand steady, and turn the iron tongs slightly. The depth at which you burn should be about half the thickness of the skin. Then lift your hand to prevent burning the vein below, which could cause bleeding. Afterwards, soak a cotton pad in salt water and place it on the area, leaving it for three days. Then apply the cotton with oil, then treat it with the ointment until it heals by the will of God.
And if you wish, iron the blister with the point of the sharp scissors taken from the iron, and take care to avoid cutting the vein in this non-chronic blister.
Fourth Chapter.
Iron the chronic blister.
If you treat the blister with the advanced treatment we have mentioned and with what we have mentioned in the sections of diseases, and the treatment does not succeed, and you see in the illness something that cannot be treated by the first branding with medicine or branding with fire. You must heat the scissor-like iron until it becomes red-hot, placing it on the spot of pain along a line about half an inch or so in length. You then withdraw your hand once and pull it firmly until you cut the vein and reach near the bone.
Except that you must be careful to avoid contacting the jaw bone, which moves during chewing; otherwise, you may burn the muscle or the nerve that controls it, causing spasms.
And be careful and vigilant about the bleeding from the vein you have cut; indeed, there is danger in cutting it. And especially for those who do not know what to do and have no tried experience; it is better to refrain from the work.
And the management of accidental bleeding from the vein will be mentioned in its proper place in the book, if God wills. If you see in the illness something that this branding cannot treat.
I have seen the diseased body capable of it placed in a cut in the middle of the head as we described and treated the wound until it heals, God willing.
And if you prefer, use the cautery which we mentioned in the chapter on straightening the artery with the tongs having two blades; for it is a better and more effective cautery than this.
The Fifth Chapter.
On the Cauterization of Ear Ailments.
If there is pain in the ear due to cold and it has been treated with laxatives and other treatment as described in the division of symptoms and the pain does not subside, heat the tongs called النقطة. Here is its image:
Then apply it around the entire ear as you circle it, or around both of them if the pain is in both. And apply the cautery a little distance from the base of the ear after marking the spot with ink. The cautery should be about ten points in each ear or close to that. Then treat the areas until it heals, God willing.
The Sixth Chapter.
On the Cauterization of Piles.
Piles that are treated with cautery are only of the type that occurs from phlegm, as described in the divisions of diseases.
And cautery should be avoided for the type that occurs from dryness and spasms of the nerve.
When you have treated this kind of abscess with poultices, fomentations, and incisions without success, it should be cauterized with three cauteries. One at the base of the ear and the second slightly below his cheekbone and the third at the meeting of the lips.
Make your cautery from the opposite side of the affected area, for relaxation only occurs in the healthy appearing side.
A diagram of the cautery should be a cauterization made opposite the top ear tip beneath the skull slightly, and another on the cheek, with its length being the same as the upper arm.
Lower your hand with the cautery until it burns to half the thickness of the skin. This is a diagram of the cautery, which is a type of septic instrument, though a bit gentler as you can see. It should have a slightly thickened edge, then treat the area as previously described until it heals, by the grace of God.
Seventh Chapter.
On the Cauterization of Chronic Hemorrhoids.
If the hemorrhoids have persisted and your treatment as described has been ineffective, and there is no fever in the affected area, cauterize it with four cauteries. On each side of his head, a cautery, and one in the middle of the head as previously mentioned, and one at the back of the head.
Recipe for the cauterization as described above, and it can also be seared with a hot iron at the mouth of the stomach, which would be more effective, then treated as previously mentioned.

Which is caused by phlegm, it should first be given decoctions of the large roots and pure brain-tonifying herbs.
Then, his head should be shaved completely, and a compress of dill, as written in the article on compresses, should be applied to the back of his neck. Apply it several times, as it is a form of cauterization.
And do it in the same sequence as I mentioned there; if he is cured thereby, well and good. Otherwise, apply three cauterizations to the back of his head, arranged from the top of the head to the bottom of the neck.
And make the interval between each cauterization one fingerbreadth. Then treat each cauterization with the remedies mentioned above. If you wish to increase the treatment and the patient can tolerate it, apply the middle cauterization.
If you wish to increase the treatment, apply it to the horns as well. Then treat him until he is cured. The cauterization should be oil-based and in the manner previously described.
第九章。
In the cauterization for the falaj and relaxing all parts of the body.
It should first be treated by purging the head with decoctions as mentioned. Then shave the patient's head. Next, cauterize the center of the head with one cauterization, and apply cauterizations to each crown of the head, and also to the back of the neck.
And for three vertebrae of the neck, if in a disease of relaxation of the body you need more than that and the patient is capable of it and the disease is strong and persistent, give him four cauterizations on his vertebras of the back. And apply the cauterization until it burns more of the skin and then raise your hand. Then treat it as mentioned earlier until it heals, if God wills it, and let the iron be oily.
The Tenth Chapter.
On the Cautionary Treatment of Epilepsy.
Only the epileptic who has epilepsy due to phlegm should be cauterized. It is best to cleanse his brain first with hot applications and with all the treatment we have mentioned in the division if the patient is large and capable of taking medicines.
If, however, he is a child who cannot take medicines, let hot applications and brain-cleansing compresses be used before that for many days, along with improving his diet.
Then shave his head, and apply the single cauterization in the middle of the head as described in the procedure, and another one at the back. And for each horn of his head, apply one cauterization. If the patient is strong and capable, give him the cauterizations mentioned in the chapter on relaxation of the body at the vertebrae of the neck and the vertebrae of the back. Let the iron be oily as described earlier.
If the patient is a child, make the iron gentle as described.
The Twelfth Chapter.
In the Correction of the Malnkhulia.
If the cause of malnkhulia is corrupt humors and thick phlegm, use the cauterizations we mentioned in the case ofفالج.
If the cause of malnkhulia is an excess倾向 towards black bile, and the patient's body is moist and corrupt, use what has been mentioned earlier on in the classification for cleansing his brain.
Then shave the patient's head. Then make a tight circular patch of cloth. Place it in the center of his head while the patient is seated and supported, holding it from all sides. Then take one pound of old sheep tallow.
Then heat it on the fire with a moderate heat, as much as an finger can tolerate when inserted. Empty it into the center of his head in the circle, and let it cool. Do this to the patient once a week along with all other good management until he is cured, if God wills it.
And if you wish, prick it with many small cauterizations without holding the iron. Instead, let it be a branding. For this type of cauterization moistens the brain moderately.
Then apply a cloth soaked in tallow or chicken fat to it.
The Twelfth Chapter.
In the Correction of Water Running into the Eye by Cauterization.
If it becomes apparent to you at the beginning of water flowing into the eye according to the signs mentioned in the division, hasten to apply the procedure for easing the discomfort and cleanse his head from all moistures and bathe him in the bath before breakfast for several days.
Then shave his head and make a cut in the middle of the head. Make two cuts on the cheeks if the water began to flow in both eyes or from one side. If it began in one eye, make the cuts accordingly.
Then cut with the cautery all the veins and arteries under the skin, and let the cuts be long in width across the cheeks, preserving from bleeding.
If you see anything of it, cut it out on the spot with any treatment at your disposal. We will address the method in separating and cutting the veins and preserving from bleeding next.
And it may be necessary to make two strong cuts under the cheekbones with the cautery.
The Thirteenth Section.
On Curing Chronic Tears.
If the tears from the eye are chronic and constant, and they come from the veins and arteries in front of the head outside the skull, and you are certain that this is due to cold, thick, phlegm-related congestion, make the cut for cauterization as described for the beginning of water flowing into the eye. Cut in the middle of the head, make two cuts on the cheeks, and make two cuts under the cheekbones. If you need to increase it, make a cut at each side of the eye near the eyebrow with a small cautery.
The Fourteenth Chapter.
In Correction of the Nasal Septum.
If the treatment as described in the division did not succeed, proceed with applying Cucumis colocynthis three days, then shave his head and perform the central cauterization with the oil-soaked iron. Then cauterize with the wooden iron two times above the eyebrows slightly below the hairline, taking care to protect the blood vessel and not cut it. This is the image of the wooden iron.
The Fifteenth Chapter.
In Cauterization for Relaxed Eyelid.
If the eyelid is relaxed due to a disease or moisture, cauterize it once with this semicircular iron.
And if you wish, cauterize above the eyebrows slightly, two times in each direction, keeping a distance from the cheeks. The length of each cauterization should be equal to the length of the eyebrow.

The Sixteenth Chapter.
In Cauterization of the Eyelid.
If the eyelids turn inward, first evert the eye, and cauterize it in two types of manner. Either cauterize with fire or with a burning medicinal solution. If cauterizing with fire, you should instruct the patient to refrain from touching their eyelids if they are of those who pluck them, until they grow long and even.
If the wound is near a plant, tie his eyes with a bandage so that they do not move until it grows. If it grows and becomes stable, place the patient's head on your lap and teach him on the eyelid with ink a mark in the shape of a leaf.
The mark should begin near the eyelid margin. Then place a cotton cloth soaked in egg white or dragon's saliva under the eyelid. Afterwards, protect and fix this shape with a mold.
Then mold it to the shape you taught it gradually many times until the surface of the skin, which is in the form of a leaf of aspen, burns completely. A sign that your work is correct is seeing the eyelid lift and the hair rise from the flesh around the eye.
Then raise your hand and leave it for three days, then apply a cotton cloth soaked in oil until the scab falls off. Then treat it with ointment until it heals, if God wills. If any hair grows back after some time and the eyelid relaxes, treat it accordingly.
Then reapply the cauterization to that area as you did first. If the hair is on the lower eyelid, pluck it until it returns to its natural position without making the eye look asymmetrical. As for cauterization with a burning drug, you should order the patient to keep the eyelid open, allowing it to stretch and become even.
Then make a paper image of an aspen leaf. Take from the common soap and from the unextinguished lime, from each one, a weight of a dirham or about that. Crush them all well and do this quickly to prevent them from drying out. Then spread it on the paper you have made in the shape of a date leaf and place it over one or both eyelids. Place under the eye a cotton cloth soaked in egg white and hold the radula in your hand.
Then place your middle finger over the medicine and press it slightly, moving it whenever the radula feels the taste of the medicine because it finds in it a taste like fire. As long as it finds the taste, leave the medicine and move it with your finger. When the taste subsides, remove the medicine and wash the eye with water.
And look, if you see the eyelid has lifted up as it does when tightened by heat or cutting, then reapply the medicine to the place where the medicine did not take effect and did not become black until you complete your work and tighten the eye. Then put on it cotton soaked in oil until the burning sensation subsides.
Then treat it with the date ointment or another, until it heals. It is essential when working that you be as careful as possible to ensure nothing of the medicine falls into the eye, for if the eyelid relaxes after days and we fear hair might have entered the eye.
Then reapply the medicine to that place where the eyelid has relaxed, specifically as you did at first. Then treat it until it heals. This is an image of a date leaf.
Know that people's eyes may differ in size and age, so adjust your technique accordingly. The correct path to success in this craft is not hidden from those who have experience with it.
Seventeenth Chapter.
In the correction of the hump in the cheek which appears in eye inflammation.
If you have treated the hump with what we mentioned in the divisions of diseases and the treatment was ineffective, it should be cauterized in this manner.
You should direct the patient to place his head on your lap and hold his head with a servant between your hands so that it does not move or strike with his head.
Then place a wet cloth on his eyelids, either in the white of an egg or in the saliva of a gecko. Then heat the iron, which is shown in this image.
It should be hollow, shaped like one end of an owl's feather tube, with the burning iron inserted at that end. If you prefer, it can have a开口的另一端。否则，可以做成静止的状态，如同纺锤一般。不过，这种一端开口的形式更适合你的需要，愿上帝愿意。
Then squeeze the hump if it is open and remove the mada (a kind of pus) from it, then dry it. If it is not open, you should make it open and extract its pus. Then place the heated iron on it, holding it with your hand until it reaches the bone.
And withdraw your hand a little during the cauterization from the eye towards the nose to avoid误操作或使患者不安，导致铁器误入眼耳软骨，损坏它。如果在第一次烧灼时铁器已达到骨头，则无需再次放置铁器；否则，如需再次放置，请这样做。
Leave it for three days, then apply a cloth soaked in oil and treat it with the dried ointment until it heals. If it does not heal after forty days, apply the corrosive medicine until the bone becomes visible, and then proceed as will be described in its section,愿上帝愿意。
Another aspect of the shaping of the gourd, mentioned by some early authors, is to aim at the place of the gourd and incise it, then place a thin plug in the same incision. This is its appearance.
You should pour into it a quantity weighing a dirham of melted tin and hold your hand with the plug firmly and tightly sealed so that the diseased part does not move at all lest the melted tin flow into his eye. It is best to place on the eye of the diseased part a cloth soaked in egg white or water.
If the tin burns the place of the gourd and cures it wonderfully, then if the gourd is cured as mentioned by cauterization and treatment, there is no need for using a nasal puncture and returning the gourd to the nasal passage as will be discussed in its specific place.
Eighteenth Chapter.
In the cauterization of cleft lip.
Often a cleft occurs in the lip and is called a "hair" cleft, particularly in boys' lips, as it frequently happens. If this cleft is treated with the division method as mentioned and the treatment is ineffective, heat a small steel awl on this image.
Its interior should be heated until it becomes as soft as a steel awl. Then place it hot on the cleft, until the cauterization reaches the depth of the cleft. Then treat it with cerate until it heals, God willing.
Nineteenth Chapter.
In Repairing the Sharp Crack in the Mouth.
If a swelling appears in the root of the gums or in the cheek or in the roots of the teeth, then it becomes pus-filled and bursts, causing a sharp crack, and treatment is ineffective, it should be covered with a splint to fit the size of the crack.
Then introduce a hot iron into the hole of the crack and hold your hand until the iron is securely inserted to its depth, doing this one or two times, then treat it with the remedies we have mentioned until it heals, if Allah wills.
If the material is exhausted and it heals, then there is no need for further examination. Otherwise, it is necessary to examine the place and remove the rotten bone as will be described in its section, if Allah wills.
Chapter Twenty.
In Repairing the Teeth and Relaxed Gums.
If the gums become relaxed due to moisture and the teeth have moved, treat them with medications. If it does not improve, place the affected area in your hand, then heat the splint that will be described after placing the tube on the tooth.
And introduce the splint, which is heated with the firewheel, into it. Hold your hand for a moment so that the affected area feels the heat has reached the root of the tooth. Then remove your hand and reinsert the splint several times as desired. Finally, fill the affected area's mouth with salt water.
And hold it for a while, then discard it. The移动指令似乎出现了中断，我将继续翻译剩余的部分：
The Twenty-First Chapter.
In the Extraction of Pain in the Tooth.
If the toothache is due to cold or there is worm in it and medical treatment does not help, extraction can be done in two ways: either by extracting with oil or by extracting with fire.
As for the extraction with oil, you should take bull's oil, boil it in an iron pot or a ladle, then take a cotton ball and wrap it at the end of the rod. Dip it in the boiled oil and apply it to the affected tooth using the wheel, holding it until it cools down.
Then, repeat it several times until the heat of the fire reaches the root of the tooth. If you prefer, you can dip a cotton ball or a piece of wool in cold oil and apply it to the affected tooth, placing an iron tool heated on top of it until the heat reaches the bottom of the tooth.
And as for extraction with fire, you should use a copper or iron tube with some thickness to prevent the heat of the fire from reaching the patient's mouth. Then, heat an iron press (the tool used for this method), place it on the same tooth, and hold your hand until the iron press cools down. Repeat this several times.
For the pain will go either on that very day or another day. It is advisable after this extraction to fill the patient's mouth with good oil and hold it for a while, then spit it out. This is the image of the iron press.
Kowt aw ayy taf shait wa ala al-ḥusb al-ladha kana bihi, wa hādhā ṣifrah al-anbūbah.
The Twenty-Second Chapter.
In Kowt al-khanāzir.
If the pigs are due to phlegm and cold moisture and do not respond to maturation by medicines, and you desire quick maturation, heat the hollow iron fork, which is shown in this image with its two ends perforated.
Let the smoke arise from the other end when branding. Place it protected over the same swelling once or twice if needed until you reach the depth of the swelling. If the swelling is small, keep the iron fork at the size of the swelling.
Then leave it for three days and apply a cotton soaked in oil. When the burned area is gone, treat it with ointments and fomentations until it heals, if God wills.
The Twenty-Third Chapter.
In branding for hoarseness and narrowness of the windpipe.
If the moisture predominates in the windpipe, especially if there is also a cold temperament, it should first be induced to vomit with purgative medicines. Then brand it by branding in the notch of the neck at the base of the throat in the lower location.
Be careful not to reach the throat with the branding, and only burn a quarter of the skin. Then brand another time at the shoulder joint near the end of one of its large veins. The iron fork should be of the same shape as previously described.
Then treat it with what has been previously mentioned until it heals by the will of God.
The Fourth and Twenty-Fourth Chapter.
On the Cough and Disease of the Lung.
If the cough and disease of the lung are due to cold dampness and there is no fever or chills, and if the illness is chronic, apply two keiyas above the trachea in the low, soft, empty places and another keiya in the middle of the chest between the breasts.
And the keiya should be in the form of a nail as previously described. If you prefer, it can be a puncturing keiya using the point-like keiya known as النقطة (nabqat al-naqd). Its shape was previously shown for puncturing pain in the ears, and the points should consist of about thirty needles.
Then treat it with what has been previously mentioned until it heals. You can make a keiya with three branches in this form and hasten the treatment, as you will be applying three keiyas in one session. This is the shape of the keiya.
The Twenty-Fifth Chapter.
On the Keiya of the Elbow.
If the head of the elbow dislocates due to slippery dampness, or if it does not remain stable after reducing it from its dislocation until it becomes habitual and then dislocates with the slightest movement as we have witnessed, it should first be reduced. Then, place the patient on their back or on the correct side. Raise the skin inside the elbow with your left hand fingers if the joint dislocated inward.
Then protect the two-pronged tongs, its image is shown here.
Then it is ironed with them until it is transferred to the other side, and the shape of the ironing will be four wrinkles. It may be ironed with a three-pronged tongs, making the shape of the ironing six wrinkles, and the prongs will be on the delicate part.
This is the image of the three-pronged tongs.
And an additional one may be added to this number, making the wrinkles eight. Then apply the curved stamped balls with salt, and bind the weak part well, so that the organ is not moved for a while until it strengthens. If the dislocation is upwards, this rarely happens.
Place one good round wrinkle or many wrinkles with punctures above the iliac crest. The joint will tighten, and the moisture will be eliminated, causing the weak part to heal.
The Sixth and Twenty-sixth.
On ironing the stomach.
If the stomach suffers from cold and excessive moisture, causing it to deviate from its normal state, and there is an increase in secretions, and various treatments have been applied but without success, it should be laid on its back with its legs and arms extended, and then ironed three times. Iron it with a round tongs under the handle of the chest, as wide as one finger. Iron it twice below each side of the single iron, so that the shape of the irons forms a triangle and keep the distance between them to prevent them from meeting if they become inflamed. The depth of the ironing should be two-thirds the thickness of the skin, and the shape of the irons should be maintained.
On this picture and to this extent only.
And if you choose, make it with one large incision in the middle of the stomach as shown in this picture.
And the iron used to make this single incision should be circular as shown in this picture.
And the stomach may be punctured with points for those who are afraid of this incision. It is done by marking points on the part you desire with a pen, then ironing it with a point-making iron, and then treating it with the aforementioned treatment until he recovers.
The Twenty-Seventh Chapter.
On the Incision of the Cold Liver.
If one complains of liver pain due to cold and dampness or from a fermentation gas until it has altered its natural temperament excessively, and the treatment for the affected part as mentioned in the division of treatments did not prove effective. It is necessary that the affected part be laid on its back and three incisions be made with a pen in this shape and to this extent on the liver below the ribs, where the human arm ends.
And after each incision, make another incision on the base of the thumb. The incisions should be straight along the length of the body. Do not hold the iron tightly with your hand.
Let the iron burn through to half the thickness of the skin no more. The affected part should be standing on its feet; if it cannot stand, let it lie with its legs stretched out and its arms raised. This is the shape of the iron.
And you may cauterize these vessels with the scalpel iron if you have a companion and skill in the craft and take care lest you delve into the cauterizing and burn all the skin, burning the belly and reaching the intestines; for the skin there is thin, so know it.
The Twenty-Eighth Chapter.
On the Swelling of the Liver with Cauterization.
If a boil appears in the liver and you want to know whether this swelling is in the liver flesh or in the bile duct, then if it is in the liver flesh, he will find the lesion heavy and painful but not sharp.
And if it is in the bile duct, then along with the pain there will be a severe sharpness. I have found that this has baffled the physicians in its treatment; therefore, the lesion should be placed on its back, then learn about the warm area using ink.
Then heat the iron in the fire; this is the scalpel-like iron, and here is its shape. And cauterize it with one pass of the iron until it burns all the skin and ends the cauterization at the bile duct until the cord is completely removed, then treat it with boil remedies until it heals.
And this type of cauterization should be used only by one who has a long training in the craft of medicine and has frequently handled such cases through experience; then he may undertake such work, but leaving it to me would be better.
The Twenty-Ninth Chapter.
In Treatment of Scrofula.
The ancients used the treatment of scrofula with the root of zraund. They took one long, dry root, longer than they could find, and made it like a thumb. Then they immersed it in oil and heated it over fire. Then apply one cautery between the connection of the clavicle and the neck, and two small cauteries below the armpits slightly towards the area under the chin. Apply two large cauteries above the breasts between the third and fourth ribs.
And apply two more cauteries between the fifth and sixth ribs, slightly towards the back. Apply one additional cautery in the middle of the chest, and another above the stomach. Place three cauteries from behind, one between the shoulders, and two on the sides of the sternum below the cautery between the hands.
And your hand should not delve deep with the cautery; it should only cause a burn on the surface of the skin. Some ancients mentioned that some people used an iron shoe-like clamp and would protect it to insert it between the ribs until it reached the affected lump.
The treatment duration is as we mentioned for a liver tumor. In this case, using the cautery on the boil can either result in the patient's death at that moment, or leave a fistula with no chance of healing.
The Thirtieth Chapter.
In Treatment of the Liver.

On the liver clips which present their shape, and there should be between each clip and clip a thickness of about the breadth of a finger or a little more, and the iron of the clamp shall have the form we mentioned for clipping the liver. Do not delve your hand deeply into the clipping, and the patient is laid on his back.
The other side is in the armpit and the skin above the liver is raised where the arm of the patient ends. The skin above the liver where the left arm ends is also raised. Your raising of the skin should be as wide as the body so that the clips fall along the length of the body.
Then you insert the tongs carefully protected so that they penetrate the skin from the other side. Then you remove the three-pronged clamp, making the clips four. If you wish to sear with the other clamp with four prongs.
Then treat the site of the clip after you leave it to drain pus for many days, for this is more effective than all that has been mentioned before in treatment.
The thirty-first chapter.
On clipping for hydrocele.
Clipping is effective only in hydrocele of the testicle, specifically. If you treat the patient with the various treatments mentioned in our classification and it does not improve, it should be clipped with four clips around the scrotum and one clip on the stomach.
And one clip on the liver and one on the spleen. Two clips behind his back between the vertebrae, one close to his chest and another close to his stomach. The depth of the clip should be about the thickness of the skin. Then you leave the clip open, allowing the pus to drain for a long time.
Do not neglect the diseased part in treatment after cauterization by what is appropriate for it, so that those who are meant to gather may hasten recovery. And the shape of the tongs used to cauterize the back shall be corkscrew-shaped as has been previously described, and the one used to cauterize the back shall be oil-filled.
The Thirty-Second Chapter.
On cauterizing the feet and legs.
If they swell in the edema and are filled with yellow water, it should be cauterized on the heel between the thumb and the forefinger.
And hold your hand with the tongs without bending it, then lift your hand and do not return it at all, for this will cause the yellow water to drain, and the tongs should be held in this shape.
Then cauterize the legs with two cauterizations on each leg. The cauterization should be made with the sharp end of the tongs along the length of the leg, one below the knee and another lower, near the middle of the leg. On each thigh, perform two cauterizations as well.
And leave the cauterization open without treatment for a long time until the yellow water drains from it, then treat it with whatever we have mentioned.
The Thirty-Third Chapter.
On cauterizing diarrhea.
If the diarrhea is due to cold and moisture, weakening the grasping and digestive powers in the stomach and intestines, and this has been treated with various remedies without success, and you find that the patient is capable of cauterization and has sufficient strength, then perform a large cauterization on his stomach. On what precedes in ironing the stomach with the circular iron and four irons around the navel, apply the gentle clasp iron and large iron on cotton over the omentum or two irons.
If you find the discharges abundant and the patient able to tolerate it, apply an iron on the scrotum and an iron on each thigh. Sometimes I added two small irons over the stomach near the large one; for it is a successful treatment whose benefit never fails by the will of Allah.
The Fourth and Thirty-Third Chapter.
On Ironing for Prolapsed Hemorrhoids.
If in the hemorrhoids there are chronic prolapsed hemorrhoids, many or one, and they are tough, cold, or bad discharges, and after treating them as mentioned in the division, the treatment was not effective, apply the gentle iron three times at the bottom of the spine below the waist slightly triangular.
Apply an iron below the navel about the size of two fingers. If you estimate that his stomach has cooled and his food does not digest, and I see his face swollen, apply a large iron on the stomach as previously mentioned, and one on his liver. And another on his spleen with a clasp iron. Leave the ironing open for some time, then treat him until he recovers, by the will of Allah.
The Fifty-Third Chapter.
On Ironing Thrombophlebitis.
After cutting it, if the cornu copiae is cut, heat the tongs resembling a claw, then insert them hot into the same cornu copiae that was cut and keep your hand there until the tongs reach the mouth of the vein from which the blood flows. Do this once or twice.
If the warts are many, cauterize each one separately as described, then treat them with ointments suitable for them until they heal. If his cautery is a large cauterization on cotton, it is more beneficial.
The Sixty-Third Chapter.
For the cauterization of the navel and its surroundings.
If the disease does not respond to the incision and the work we described in its place, and he becomes weak in that, it may heal by cauterization. If this happens to any navel and pus and foul moisture occur, the first thing you should do is measure it with a fine probe.
Then measure its depth with a fine probe. Heat the tongs resembling a claw, then insert them hot into the navel at the same depth as the probe entered and in the same straight line. Repeat the cauterization once or twice or three times according to your need until all those foul substances are burned.
And take care to avoid burning the nerve if there is one, or a large vein. If the navel opens into the bladder or the intestine.
And take care with all these places. You do this only if the navel is in a place that can heal and you have determined that it is not infected, then treat the area until it heals. If I cauterized the area and the discharges ceased and it remained so for some time, know that it has healed completely.
And if the materials do not cease from it, know that it is efficacious or there is a defect in a bone within its depth or something similar to what will be mentioned in its place.
The Thirty-Seventh Chapter.
On the Treatment of the Kidney.
If pain occurs in the kidney due to cold or a strong foul smell, and there is a decrease in seminal emission, it should be cauterized on the flanks over the same kidney, seared for each kidney with the clamp mentioned earlier. It might have been cauterized a third time on the same plate, resulting in three consecutive cauterizations, which would be more effective in benefiting the condition.
The Thirty-Eighth Chapter.
On the Treatment of the Bladder.
If the bladder shows weakness and relaxation due to cold and dampness, such that it cannot retain the seminal fluid, cauterize it with a burnisher at the bottom of the pubic region where the pubic hair begins. Also, cauterize another one on the right side and another on the left side of the pubic region.
It should be cauterized from each side to the extent of a thumb's knot. Cauterize it at the lower back with one burnisher, or two if necessary, and use the clamp type mentioned earlier.
The Thirty-Ninth Chapter.
On the Treatment of the Uterus.
If the uterus is affected by materials due to cold and dampness, it will become unable to conceive, and its texture will be impaired, making conception difficult. Alternatively, if pain occurs with its onset, it should be cauterized three times around the pubic region, as we mentioned in the treatment of the bladder. The Forty-Third Chapter.
Kiyya takhlu al-wark.
Qad tnisab ruteebat makhyyata ila haq al-wark fa takuna saba' l-khuruj alaynahu mu'alla. Walaa'mahu an tattalul saaqi al-aththaara idha qastu bintihaa illa bihā watadkhul muważza al-khulūf fīnhunabighā allakawā al-'ilil 'ala haq al-wark al-ḥimma kiyata shibah ad-dā'ira.

The Forty-First Chapter.
Kiyya 'irr al-naswa.

If it extends to the thigh and leg, burn two on the thigh at the position indicated by the patient's pain. One above the greater trochanter by four fingers towards the outer side slightly, and let the iron be of a knife-like shape. The depth of the burn should be only the thickness of the skin.

Then treat it with ointments until he recovers. If the pain extends to the thigh or leg, make a mold as you did for the hip according to its size. This is the formula for hot water, and I have established it in an article on the restoration of medicines.

And pour sweet water over the salt and lime enough to cover them with an inch, after wetting them well with your hand. Leave the pot until the hot water settles in the thickened bottom pot. Then collect all that water, and pour it over fresh lime and new salt, repeating the process.
Then it will be very sharp, acting in many medical procedures and in the cauterization of all organs, for it does what fire itself does. Some medicines also serve to cauterize the hip, such as thafsiya, honey from palm date flowers, and a mixture of lime and soap that has been boiled.
Galen related a remedy for pain in the hip and women's diseases from ancient times, and he greatly praised its efficacy, claiming that it is not necessary to use any other treatment, and that it cures in one application.
It might even be carried to the bathhouse in a container and come out cured after one application. And wrap it and leave it for three hours or until the patient feels the burning sensation subside. Then, take him to the bathhouse; if his body is refreshed, immerse him in a basin. He heats it with fire until it becomes a glowing coal, then places it on the cotton and leaves it until it extinguishes. Then take another, and do thus until the sense reaches the middle of the arm to the hip, and the pain subsides by God's leave. This kind of cauterization is called cauterization of the bura'.
The Forty-Second Chapter.
On Cauterization of Pain in the Back.
Pain in the back may occur due to many causes, such as a fall or a blow or excessive vomiting, and so on. It is caused by the accumulation of cold, wet material. Cauterization is applied only in this type.
Which is caused by the accumulation of cold material. It should be applied after vomiting with safflower or similar substances, cauterizing three rows on the area of the back where the pain is, each row as wide as a table. In each row, apply five cauterizations or more according to what you see in terms of the severity and strength of the patient's condition.
The cauterization should be done with a point iron. Alternatively, you can use three or four medium-sized nail irons on this pattern.
The Forty-Third Chapter.
On Cauterization of the Beginning of Hump Formation.
This condition often affects young children. Its onset in a child can be identified by observing difficulty in breathing during standing and movement. You may also find a protruding bead at the end of the vertebrae that stands out from the other beads.
If you see that and wish to stop it, apply with a tongs being circular in this shape. Take the cautery on every side of the vertebra equally. If you wish, apply it around the vertebra with a tongs having two or three points, let the points be close to one another. Then treat the area until it heals as we have mentioned.
And be careful not to use the cautery on the hump that occurs from nerve spasms.
The Fourth and Forty- fourth Chapter.
On the Cautery for Gout and Joint Pain.
If the joint pain is due to cold dampness affecting any part of the body, if the pain occurs in the legs, it is customary for physicians to call this gout specifically.
If the cold dampness causing gout does not respond to the treatments we have mentioned in the classification, and the pain persists, then cauterization can relieve it. This involves applying the cautery around the ankles after vomiting, using many cauterizations with a medium oil-based tongs as shown in this shape.
And if you need to prick the leg, do so with a point tongs. If the pain ascends to the knees or to other joints, and this often occurs, apply four or five cauterizations on each knee from every side using this same oil-based tongs.
If you need more cauterizations beyond this, apply them without deepening your application with the cautery; it should be about the thickness of the skin only. If the pain ascends to the hips or to the back, use what we have mentioned for cauterization in its section.
If the pain is only in the hands, puncture around the wrist as two circles. If the pain remains in the fingers, puncture each joint with a point and the hand comb. If the pain ascends after days to the elbows or armpits.
Puncture from every direction. No lesion is without good management and taking medicines. For if the food is well and the phlegm is expelled, it will be cured with this burning if God wills.
The Fifty-fourth Chapter.
In Puncturing the Foreskin.
If a fistula occurs in the rectum and some intestine or pus has descended to the scrotum, and this is a recent beginning, it should be ordered that the patient abstain from food for a day and use laxatives to help expel the feces from his bowels.
Then he should lie before you on his back and be ordered to hold himself until the pus or intestine protrudes, then push it back with your finger. Then mark with ink under the fistula on the sacrum a mark shaped like half a circle, its ends going upwards towards the body.
Then heat the iron to make its image.
Until a white substance throws out sparks, then push the intestine or pus back into his bowels. Then place a servant's hand on the area to prevent the intestine from protruding again. Having relieved between the legs of the patient and placed a pillow under him, put another servant on his feet.
And another on his chest, holding his hands, then the iron is placed on the mark itself and you stand straight with it and hold it until you reach the bone with it or redo it once if you did not reach it the first time to the bone.
And you preserve your effort to prevent the protrusion of the intestines while cauterizing lest you burn him, and thereby happens to the patient either death or a great disability. And know that your cauterization is not successful if you do not reach the bone with it. It is advisable that the iron for boys be gentle according to their size and for adults according to their size.
Then treat the place of cauterization with oil after three days until the blackness of the burn disappears, then treat it with other ointments until he recovers. Let the patient lie on his back for forty days until the wound is covered.
And you should make his food during his treatment such that it softens his belly lest the intestines protrude at defecation and urination. Then, when he wishes to get up after forty days, use a tight belt for forty days more, reducing his exertion, overfilling with food and drink, and loud shouting.
If he is treated this way, he will recover completely, God willing. I will mention the treatment for inguinal hernia by making an incision in its opening, God willing. As for the hernia that occurs elsewhere in the belly and is new, if you want it not to increase, treat it with a circular cauterization of its size. Let what you burn of the skin be like two-thirds of it, then treat it as we have mentioned. For it will not increase, God willing. Some early practitioners have also advised cauterizing the hernia with a triangular iron.
After learning the technique for hernia with ink and making the line at the upper side of the hernia and another line below, place your scalpel in the middle. The first cautery is easier and better, God willing.
The Sixty-Fourth Chapter.
In cauterizing the throta.
If pain occurs in some organs due to a fall or blow and this pain persists for a long time and does not respond to medical treatment, it should be cauterized with a cautery point. The cautery should be applied according to the size and strength of each organ.
And if the pain and swelling subside from the first cautery, it is cured by the first cautery. Otherwise, reapply the cautery because it is common for such pains to spread to what is nearby. You should follow up with another cautery until the disease is cured.
The Forty-Seventh Chapter.
On Cauterizing Leprosy.
As for leprosy sufferers, they may benefit greatly from cauterization, especially the type that results from the putrefaction of phlegm and black bile.
If you intend to cauterize it, first observe whether the leprosy is new and treated it as described in the classification. If it did not subside or stop and you fear that the disease might corrupt all his humors, then cauterize him on the head with five cautery treatments. The one in the middle of the head, the common one and the second below it toward the forehead at the end of the hair and two on the corners and one behind at the prominence of the forehead and apply your hand gently with the hammer until it affects the bone slightly.
And the crusts peel off, making it easier for the vapors to pass through and for cauterization with the hammer in the same manner as the liver, as previously mentioned. If the leprosy has continued on the healthy part and a clear appearance has shown, then it should be cauterized with these hammer burns we have mentioned on the head. Cauterize the tip of the nose with one burn, two on the cheeks, two on the cervical vertebrae, six on the lumbar vertebrae, one large one at the hyoid bone when the penis fails, and another above it on the same table. Two on the hips, one on each hip. Two on the knees, one on each knee, two on the elbows, two on the armpits, two on the wrists, and cauterize each joint of his fingers and toes with a burn. Also, cauterize each heel of his feet and brand his hands.
Protect the nerve at the back of the heels so as not to burn them. You may cauterize one burn on the pubic bone, another on the opening of the stomach, and another on the liver. Know that the more burns you apply, the better and more effective it will be.
Know that the healthy part does not feel pain from cauterization as much as the diseased part because its body is numbed. The size of the irons for cauterization should be appropriate to the organs and joints according to the previously mentioned qualities of the metals.
Then treat the scald with the powder of Cress and honey and all other treatment until he recovers by the will of Allah.
The Forty-First Chapter.
In scalds of the excoriated part, when a limb is scorched and treated with medicines and ointments but does not recover, then let the same limb be cauterized with scalding irons according to what the bone of the limb deserves or its smallness. Let the scalding be intense in the thickness of the skin somewhat.
Then treat it with ointment until it recovers. It may also be cauterized for some scalds that affect the hand and foot in the vertebrae of the spine at the exit of the nerve that moves that limb, thereby removing the scald.
And none should do this except one who is knowledgeable about the anatomy of the limbs and the exits of the nerves that move the body.
The Forty-First Chapter.
On scalds of the blister.
If the blister has become old and no medical remedy has been effective in it, then cauterize it with a deeper scalding iron according to the thickness of the skin until the whiteness disappears and its color changes.
Then treat it with the powder of lentils mixed with the ointment of saffron, liver of leeches, or pigeon blood from each one part. Mix all together and apply it on a cloth and apply it to the area until it recovers.
The Fifty-First Chapter.
In regard to the cancer.
If the cancer is in its beginning stage and you wish to stop it, cauterize around it with the circle iron as you turn it. Some wise men have mentioned that it should be cauterized severely at its center. But I do not see this as advisable because I expect it to ulcerate, and I have seen this happen several times.
The correct method is to cauterize around it with a circle iron as we said, or with many small cauterizations.
The Fifty-First Chapter.
In cauterizing the dubella.
If one of the dubella has become delayed in development, either due to its being more favorably positioned or because the patient is an old man with little blood, or due to time itself; and if you wish to hasten its development, cauterize around it with many small cautery marks to incise it.
Then leave it, for it will hasten its development. If you wish to delay it by cauterization, heat the iron, which is shown in this image.
And apply it in the center of the dubella until it penetrates the skin. Let the cauterization be as shown below to facilitate the flow of pus. Then treat it as appropriate until it heals.
The Fifty-Second Chapter.
In cauterizing the aeratrix.
The aeratrix is a decay that seeks to consume the tissue, just as firewood is consumed by burning fire. If you see the aeratrix in a place where cauterization with fire is possible, heat several small and large nail tongs accordingly to the size of the area affected by the aeratrix.
Then treat it from every side until all the decay is completely eradicated and nothing remains, then leave it for three days and apply the powdered sulfur with oil to the charred areas until all the scab and all the decay fall off.
Then treat it with ointments that promote healing of the flesh. If after three days you see that the flesh is growing healthily with no decay, then proceed as necessary. Otherwise, retreat the charred areas with heat on what remains diseased. The patient should be treated with a strong remedy.
For it serves in place of fire more effectively. I have mentioned its treatment with a strong remedy in the classification; take it from there when you need it.
The Fifth and Fifty-Third Chapter.
On the retreating of hammered and unhammered nails.
This condition often occurs in the soles of the feet and is a rough object that penetrates the foot. The treatment can be performed in two ways: either by retreating it with fire or by treating it with strong water.
As for retreating it with fire, you should heat a hollow tongs resembling the quill of an eagle, made of iron to fit around the nail from every side, and make its edges thin. Then place it hot on the nail and move your hand around the nail with the tongs until the heat reaches the depth of the nail.
Then leave it for three days until the pus forms. Afterwards, apply a poultice of crushed and salted wild breadfruit to the area overnight; it will fall off from its roots. Then treat the wound with an ointment that promotes healing of the flesh until it heals, if the nails are not hammered.
Often do we find them on the surface of the body, especially in the hands and feet. It is advisable to take a pipe of brass or iron or a feather of an eagle and place it over the nail or boil. Then one should pour a little of very hot water into the pipe.
Hold your hand and direct it with a slight twitch of your wrist to affect the edge of the pipe on the root of the nail. The very hot water finds its way deep into the root of the nail, and the patient should endure the刺痛一会儿。请注意，这里翻译时使用了“刺痛”来表示原文中的“ذ卢 الماء الحادّ”，这虽然是直译，但可能需要根据上下文调整以确保准确传达原文意图。如果需要更精确的医学术语，请告知我以便进一步修改。
Then leave it. The nail will fall out with its root. Do this one by one until all of them in the body are treated, then treat the places where they have fallen out with ointments that promote flesh growth.
Chapter Forty-Five.
In Treating the Nail.
If a nail is affected by cold in the nerve or by fever for a quarter or anything else, it should be cauterized four times or five times. Use the vertebrae as a needle between each cauterization, and apply one cauterization on its chest. And apply one cauterization on its stomach with an oil-stone iron. For the nail, this calms it and speeds up the resolution of the cold disease.
Chapter Fifty-Five.
In Treating the Boil That Occurs on the Body.
It may erupt in the body pustules ugly due to cold thick corrupt substances and it should be cauterized at the first appearance of each pustule gently with a stick that has been set alight at its end or with the stem of the long zarand or with a concave iron.
And the warts may be cauterized at the first eruption in this manner; it will not increase and the beneficial effect will disappear, and the patient will recover; but it should be done after the patient vomits by emesis.
The Sixth and Fifty-First Chapter.
To cauterize the bleeding that occurs upon cutting the artery.
Frequently, bleeding from an artery occurs that has been severed by a wound from the outside or when cutting a tumor or cauterizing an organ, and it is difficult to cut it.
If any of this happens, hasten with your hand to the mouth of the artery and place your middle finger on it and draw it tight so that the blood is constricted beneath your finger and nothing escapes from it. Then take from the fire several small and large oil-soaked pincers and blow on them until they become extremely hot.
Then take one, either small or large, according to the wound and the place where the artery was severed. Place the pincers on the same vein after quickly removing your finger with the clamp and hold the pincers until the blood stops.
If the bleeding continues when you raise your finger from the mouth of the artery and extinguish the pincers, take another pair quickly from the hot pincers in the prepared fire. Continue doing this with one after another until the bleeding stops.
And take care not to burn a nerve, for if this occurs, you should treat the affected area with another ligature. Know that if a blood vessel bleeds from it, it cannot be cut, especially if the vessel is large, except in one of four ways: either by cauterization as we said, or by amputation if it has not already been severed. And if it is amputated, its ends will contract and the bleeding will cease. Either it can be tied with threads tightly, or medicines that are capable of stopping the bleeding can be applied to it, and the vessels can be pulled tight.
And as for those who attempt to stop it by tying with a bandage or pulling the veins or applying burning substances and the like, it will not cease at all except in rare cases. If such a situation arises and there is no doctor or medicine available, he should immediately place the third finger on the mouth of the wound itself, as we have described.
And pull it tightly until the bleeding stops and flows above the wound onto the vessel. The finger must remain cold with very cold water constantly to freeze the blood, thicken it, and stop it. During this time, observe whether cauterization or medicine is needed.
The Second Chapter.
On Incisions, Punctures, Incisions with Forceps, and Surgical Wounds and Similar Conditions.
Albucasis said: We have already mentioned in the first chapter all diseases that are suitable for cauterization with fire and burning medicines, and their causes and symptoms, as well as their instruments and the forms of applicators. We have made this into chapters from the thigh to the foot.
And I proceed in this matter exactly as described so that the student may easily obtain what is required.
Before I begin with this, you my sons, should know that in this chapter there is even more risk than in the first chapter concerning the cauterization.
And for this reason, the warning must be stronger, for the work in this chapter is great, and in it there often occurs the evacuation of blood from which life depends upon opening a vein or cutting into a tumor or bursting an abscess or surgical treatment or extracting an arrow or cutting into a stone, and similar things that accompany all of them risk and fear, and death occurs in most of them.
And I advise you to beware of what is doubtful to you, for in this craft various kinds of people with different afflictions may occur to you. Some may be weary of their illness and find death轻化。
And I advise you to beware of those who are severely afflicted by their sickness, suffer from the duration of their illness, and whose disease indicates death. Some may offer you their wealth in hopes of recovery, but their illness is fatal. It should not be among such people that you seek help; rather, you should avoid assisting them entirely.
And let your caution be greater than your desire and eagerness. Do not proceed with anything from this except after certain knowledge that can be verified by you leading to the praised outcome. Use in all your treatments a preliminary understanding and warning about what safety may lead to.
And indeed, you have in this the means to earn praise and glory, and be remembered and commended. May Allah guide you, my sons, to the right path and grant you correctness and success; verily, that is in His hand; there is no god but He.
And I have arranged this chapter into sections according to what was presented in the chapter on cauterization from foot to hand so that the demand of what you desire from it may be easier for you by the will of God.
The First Section.
On the Treatment of Water That Collects in the Heads of Boys.
This illness is often encountered in boys at birth if the midwife presses the child's head without gentleness. It may also occur due to a hidden cause that is unknown.
I have not seen this condition in anyone other than boys. All those I saw among them died quickly, so I therefore decided to refrain from treating it. I have also seen a boy whose head was filled with water, and the head grew larger every day. Until the boy could not sit on his own head, which had become too large, and the fluid continued to increase until he died.
And this fluid may gather between the skin and the bone, or it may collect underneath the bone on the diploe. The treatment, if the fluid is between the skin and the bone and the swelling is small, should be to make a single incision in the middle of the head, with the length of the incision about two fingerbreadths, so that the fluid may drain. This is the shape of the instrument used.
If the fluid is greater and the swelling is larger, make two intersecting incisions as shown.
And if the fluid is underneath the bone, its sign is that you see the scalp incisions open on all sides, and when you press it with your hand, the water drains inward. This should not be hidden from you; therefore, you should make three incisions in the middle of the head as shown.
After the incision, all the moisture is removed, then the incisions are tightened with sutures and ligatures. It is then treated from above with drink and oil until the fifth day. The bandage is changed, and the wound is treated with thread and ointments. The head should be tightened适度调整以符合原文意思，不添加解释）。
Until the organ strengthens and heals, another recipe for incision is to look where the bone of the tumor protrudes and the water汇聚翻译更自然，保持原文意思。）
