Urine retention in the bladder occurs due to obstruction from a stone, clotted blood, pus, or prolapsed flesh, and so on. If you treat this as described, using the methods outlined in分类，请归入其中。

When the neck of the bladder is forced to push the stone back, urine will be released. If it does not release with what we mentioned and the matter presses on the patient, it should be extracted using the instrument called catheter as shown in this figure:.
It is made of silver and is thin, smooth, and hollow like a bird's feather tube. It is about a span and a half in length. Its head has a gentle bend. To draw urine with it, take a curved thread and tie cotton or gauze securely at its end.

Chapter Sixty.
In the Extraction of Stones.
We have mentioned the classification of stones and their treatment with medicines. We have also noted the difference between a stone generated in the kidney and one generated in the bladder, along with the signs and symptoms of each. Additionally, we have discussed the stone for which manual intervention and incision are required.
And it is the stone generated in the bladder, especially that which develops in the urethra. I will describe this in detail and briefly.
I say that the stone formed in the bladder is more likely to affect boys, and one of its signs is that urine comes out of the bladder resembling water in its thinness.
Sand is visible in it, and it irritates the penis, playing with it, and often hanging down then spreading, and the prepuce becomes prominent in many of them. It is easy for boys to recover from it until they reach fourteen years, but it is more difficult in old men. As for young men, it is intermediate between the two.
And that which has a larger stone is easier to treat, while smaller stones are the opposite. When we move to treatment, it should first be that the fluid is instilled with an injection to expel all the sediment within it; for it may prevent the presence of the stone during examination.
Then, the fluid is taken with his legs and shaken downwards to cause the stone to descend into the bladder neck or to drop from a high position several times. Then, he is placed facing you with his legs hanging down, and his hands under his thighs so that the entire bladder tilts downward. Afterwards, it should be examined.
And examine it externally. If you feel the stone in the space, act quickly with your fingers to split it open. If it does not fall under your touch at all, it should be smeared with oil on the little finger if the patient is a boy, or with the middle finger.
If it is a complete boy, insert your hand into his prepuce and examine for the stone. When it falls under your finger, move it little by little to the bladder neck, then press on it with your finger and push it out towards the place you wish to incise.
And command a servant to squeeze the bladder with his hand and command another servant that he extend his right hand above towards the labia and with his other hand extend the skin beneath the labia away from the place where the incision will be, then take the forceps here is its shape.
And incise between the vulva and the labia not in the middle but beside the left labium. The incision should be of the same size as a grain of barley, with your finger inside the vulva while pressing it outward, curled so that the opening is wide on the outside and narrow on the inside to the extent that the grain of barley can pass through.
It should not be larger, for perhaps the finger inside the vulva will press the stone at the time of incision, causing it to pass out without difficulty. Know that some stones may have corners or letters, making their passage difficult due to this.
And some are smooth like acorns and rolled, making their passage easy. If it has corners or letters, increase the incision slightly. If it does not pass this way, it is best to grasp it with a clamp whose tip is like a probe.
And hold it with the clamp so that it does not escape. Alternatively, insert a thin curved instrument beneath it. If you cannot manage this, increase the incision slightly. If bleeding occurs and prevails, stop it with cauterization.
And if there are more than one, first push the largest into the bladder, then incise it, and afterward push the smaller one. Do this similarly if there are more than two. If it is extremely large, it is不明智去尝试对其施行一个极大的切口，因为这会使病人面临两种风险。
Either he dies or it happens that there is continuous dribbling of urine, for the place will not adhere at all. But try to push it until it comes out or break it with forceps until you cut it out completely.
When you have finished your work, dress the wound with a sponge and bind it tightly with bandages, stretching and tying it. Make a hole above it soaked in oil and drink or ointment and rosewater to cool the hot swelling. Then let the patient lie on his side. Do not apply the bandage until the third day.
When it has healed, wash the area with much water and oil. Then treat it with the nux vomica ointment and the basilicon ointment until it is cured. If there is a lesion in the wound and a hot swelling that increases, and similar conditions such as when blood freezes in the bladder and urine is obstructed, and this can be recognized by the discharge of blood with the urine.
Insert your finger into the wound and remove that blood, for if it remains, it may lead to corruption of the bladder and its infection. Then wash the wound with vinegar and water and salt, and treat each type with what resembles it in treatment until it is cured.
It is necessary at all times during treatment to bind the thighs together to hold the medicines applied to the area. If the stone is small and has entered the urinary tract, becoming embedded and obstructing urine flow, treat it with what I am describing before it reaches a severe stage.
Often, I have been able to use this treatment instead of making an incision. This is how you should take a wire made of ironware:
Triangle of the end sharp inserted in a stick, then take a thread and tie it under the stone so as not to return to the bladder. Then enter a forceps with care into the urethra until the forceps reaches the same stone.
Turn the forceps with your hand slightly in the same stone and aim for its hole until you pass it from the other side. Then clamp your hand on what remains of the stone outside the penis; it will break and come out with the urine, and the disease will be cured.
If this treatment is not available to you due to some obstruction, tie a thread under the stone and another above the stone. Then incise the stone in the same penis between the two ties, and remove it.
Then untie the thread and clean the congealed blood that has remained in the wound. It was necessary to tie the thread under the stone so as not to return to the bladder, and the other thread above so that when the thread is untied after the stone is removed, the skin returns to its place and covers the wound.
Therefore, when you tie the upper thread, you should raise the skin above so that it returns to its place when you are finished and covers the wound as we have said.
The Sixty-First Section.
On the Removal of Stones in Women.
Stones are rarely found in women. If a stone does develop in one of them, its treatment is difficult and often impossible due to several reasons. One reason is that the woman might be a virgin, and another is that you might not find a woman willing to allow a physician to examine her.
If she is a virgin or one of those with close kinship, and you do not find a woman skilled in this craft, especially by hand, and fourthly, since the place for making an incision for stone in women is far from the actual location of the stone, it requires a deep cut.
If there is danger in this, and necessity demands it, you should take a skilled female physician. Such women are rare, so if unavailable, seek a virtuous and gentle male physician or prepare a skilled midwife who is well-versed in matters of women. Alternatively, get a woman who can make some indication in this craft.
Prepare her and command her to perform all that you instruct her to do in examining the stone. This is that she should examine whether the woman is a virgin, for it should be that she insert her finger into the woman's vagina and feel for the stone. If she finds it and presses on it with her finger, it will give indication of its presence.
Then command her to make the incision, provided she is not a virgin but a woman of experience. Instruct the midwife to insert her finger into the patient's vagina and feel for the stone after placing her left hand on the bladder and squeezing it well.
Then, if she finds it, she should introduce it from the bladder's opening downward until she reaches the base of the thigh. There, make an incision on the side of the vagina at the base of the thigh where the stone is felt.
And her finger should not be removed from the stone, pressed beneath it. Let the incision initially be small. Then introduce a probe into this small incision. If she feels the stone, widen the incision according to what she knows is necessary for the stone to pass through. Know that types of stones are numerous.
From the small and large, smooth and rough, long and short, corkscrew-shaped and those with branches; know their kinds so that you may rely on this for what you need. If the blood overcomes you, dust it in the sticky powdered area and hold it for a while until the blood ceases, then return to your work.
Until the stone comes out, work that you may count upon among the instruments mentioned for removing stones from men to assist you in your task. If bleeding overcomes you and you know by the pulse of the blood that it is from a severed artery, place the dust on the area.
Strengthen it with ligatures tightly and leave it without redoing it. Do not remove the stone; perhaps the patient will be harmed. Then treat the wound. If the bleeding subsides after a few days and the area heals, return to your work until you remove the stone.

The Third and Sixty-Third Chapter.
On Making Incisions in the Fleshy Ligaments and Their Treatment.
Know that making incisions in these fleshy ligaments is fraught with danger, leading to death in most cases. Therefore, we see it best to avoid them and remain safe. I will, however, remember the procedure and various swellings associated with them.
I say that many swellings may occur in the bodies where the composition of the female organs is present, and this can be due to various causes: either from a hot secretion flowing into the female organs or from a blow. The color of the swelling is similar to that of the body, and it does not contain any water.
The swelling may be sore. Sometimes, the swelling becomes hard, its color like that of mud, and it has no sensation. It may also be due to the complication and swelling of the arteries, as mentioned before, or from the swelling of the veins. If the swelling is due to the swelling of the arteries, this can be recognized by the dispersion of the swelling.
If you compress it with your fingers, there should be nothing to worry about. As for what is caused by the swelling of veins, nothing disappears when compressed with fingers. This kind may cause trouble for it and for all other flesh.
And this is to incise the scrotal skin, then elevate the testis upwards and remove it through the white septum, and free the spermatic cord from the vessels, tie the vessels, and cut the spermatic cord after freeing it from all sides of the testis, if the testis has adhered to the newly grown flesh.
It is necessary to remove and cut the testis, if there is adhesion between any of the septa or among the vessels. In such cases, all such adhesions should be freed and cut in a circular manner.
If the growth of flesh is in the place of adhesion which is from behind, it is necessary to cut all of it and remove the testis as we said. When you have completed your work, dress the wound with wet cotton soaked in rose oil and wine, then treat it with other treatments until it heals.

The Fifth and Sixty-sixth Chapter.
In the Treatment of Intestinal Abscesses.
The occurrence of this abscess results from a tear that exposes the omental membrane extending over the abdomen near the ovaries. The intestine then protrudes through that hernia into one of the ovaries.
This hernia can occur either from a tear in the omental membrane or from its extension. These two types are among many causes, which may include a blow, a jump, a shout, or lifting something heavy and so on. Its sign is that it happens gradually over a long period of time if it is due to the extension of the omental membrane.
No swelling occurs suddenly and is level to the depth before the canal compresses the intestine, and its sign is that if it is from the tearing of the canal it happens from its beginning with great pain at once and the swelling is visible under the skin in the vicinity.
This occurs with the expulsion of the intestine and its exit from the canal to the outside. It may also come out with the feces, in which case it is called a mezzy disease both from the intestines and from the pus. It may also be accompanied by foul odor, and the impure material may flow into the intestine and get stuck there, causing the death of the patient.
Because it causes severe pain and cramping, especially if compressed, and the treatment of these types of ailments with iron is dangerous and should be avoided. The procedure to follow is to order the patient to push the intestine back into the abdomen with his hand if it can be returned.

The Seventh and Sixty-First Chapter.
In the hernia that occurs in the groin.
Hernia may occur in the groin as we have said, protruding the area without anything of the intestine descending into the scrotum. If any does descend, it is only a little and reverts at all times.

The Eighth and Sixty-First Chapter.
On the relaxation of the scrotal skin.
Often, the scrotal skin relaxes in some people without the flesh inside relaxing, making its appearance unpleasant. Therefore, for those who wish to treat this condition, the patient should be laid on their back.
And all the relaxed skin is cut away from the thick skin. Then join the lips, and if you wish, first suture the relaxed skin flap with three or four sutures and strengthen the suturing. Then cut between the sutures.
Then treat it according to the methods for other wounds until it heals and the sutures fall out.
Chapter Fifty-Nine
In the Male Genital Examination.
In our law, male genital examination is forbidden.
And for this reason, it is incumbent upon me not to mention it in my book. I have only mentioned it for two reasons: the first, so that it may be known to the physician if he is asked about it and so that he may know the treatment of those affected by it; the second, as we often need to examine some animals for our benefit.
As for animals such as camels, sheep, cats, and the like, I say that male genital examination occurs in two ways: either by pressing or by cutting and removing. The one done by pressing involves sitting the animal in hot water until its penis relaxes, becomes soft, and droops.
Then press it with your hand until it relaxes and does not become apparent upon touch. As for the examination by cutting and removing, you should hold the animal and squeeze the skin of its penis with your left hand, then tie the ligaments and make a single incision on each testicle.
Until the two testicles become visible, cut them after剥离它们，确保不要留下任何血管外的精索，除了附在血管上的薄精索。这种切开的方式比通过按压更为优。
Because pressing might leave something in the penis, and the animal might desire copulation. Therefore, treat the wound until it heals.
Chapter Seventy.
In the Treatment of Intersex Conditions.
The intersex condition in men occurs in two types. One of them is that it appears as a space or on the skin between the scrotum and the anus, resembling a woman's vagina with hair, and urine may flow from what is on the scrotal skin.
As for women, there is one type, which appears above the vagina on the labia, resembling small penises of men that protrude from one of them like a male penis, and both are similar to the female ones. The treatment of the three types is as follows.
For the two types in men and the single type in women, it is necessary to cut the excess flesh until its trace is removed, then treat it with the treatment of other surgeries until it heals. As for the second type in men, which discharges urine from what is on the scrotal skin, there is no need for any operation or cure at all.
The Seventy-First Chapter.
On the Cutting of the Clitoris and the Tissue Protruding from Women's Vulvas.
The clitoris may sometimes become larger than the normal size, causing it to swell and disfigure its appearance. In some women, it may enlarge to resemble that in men, making it suitable for intercourse.
It is necessary to hold the excess of the clitoris with your hand or forceps and cut it, but do not过度切割，以免引起出血。

It may sometimes come out outside like the tail. Therefore, some of the early physicians call this condition a tail abscess, and it should be cut as you would cut a balanos abscess, and it should be treated until it heals.
The Seventy-Second Chapter.
In the Treatment of Dropsy.
Dropsy is when the woman's vagina is not perforated or has a small hole, which can either be congenital or acquired. The acquired ones are due to some preceding illness and can be either from excess granulation tissue.
Or from thin or thick exudate, which can be in the depth of the uterus, on its sides, at its upper part, or lower part, and it prevents intercourse, conception, and childbirth; it might also prevent menstruation. This can be determined by the midwife's examination.
If the obstruction is visible and close, but if it is not visible, probe with her fingers or a gauze. If the obstruction is from thin exudate and close to the labia, puncture it promptly by making an incision similar to the lips, then place your thumbs on both sides.
The woman should lie on her back with her legs spread, then she should forcefully separate the labia until the thin exudate is punctured and the obstruction opens. Then she should take some wool, soak it in oil, and apply it to the area. The woman should have intercourse every day to prevent the area from adhering again.
If the sinus is thick and dense, it should be incised with a broad forceps resembling a date leaf. If the blockage is from new flesh, suspend it with forceps and cut it away; let there be with you medicines to quell bleeding without caustics such as caelia, shian, and balsam mixed with egg white.
Then use a wide lead tube lest the wound adhere quickly, hold it for days and use dry cotton wool. Then treat with other treatments for adhesion until it heals. And another mass of flesh may appear in the uterus, so it should be cut in this manner.
If it is not a malignant tumor, the malignant tumor in the uterus should not be treated with iron at all.
The Seventy-third Chapter.
In the treatment of hemorrhoids, warts, and red blisters that appear in women's genital areas.
As for hemorrhoids, they are the swelling of the openings of veins until much constant blood flows from them. When hemorrhoids become chronic, they turn into warts. I have mentioned in the classification their types, signs, and symptoms, and we will mention them here.
What can be treated and what cannot be treated, I say that hemorrhoids and warts, if they are deep in the uterus and not palpable, have no treatment with iron. Those from which there is palpation are the ones that can be treated.
It should be that the woman enter a cold room, then apply the warts with a pincette or a rough cloth, cut them off from their roots, and then sprinkle them when bleeding occurs from one of the clamps that stop the bleeding without cauterization.
Like caqia, shiyan, and laban, and similar substances. Then raise her legs to the wall for a while. Then lower them into cold water. If bleeding continues, seat her in a decoction of saffron, bark of bitter almond, and acacia gum. Take barley flour, mix it with honey and ferment.
Apply it to her back. If the bleeding stops, keep her in this position. Otherwise, use a splint for incision and mastoid areas without any exception. Then take wool and immerse it in juice of pomegranate peel or juice of pregnant tongue or juice of fig branches with acacia syrup. Keep it in place.
If the swelling subsides, treat the area with ointment until it heals. As for the red pustule, it resembles the heads of haisha, rough to look at. It should be cut where it has appeared as described in the treatments for tumors, and treated until it heals.
The Fourth and Seventy-Fourth Chapter.

Various types of tumors may occur in the womb, such as cancer, hardened tumor, ulcers, hemorrhoids, ulcerator, corns, anal fissures, warts, and hot tumor. I have mentioned all these diseases, their types, and their symptoms in the classification.

I have seen it red if sensation occurs, do not hasten to cut it but treat it with what helps maturity until these symptoms subside. Then it should be that the woman sits on a chair with two seats and supports herself on its back.
And she gathers her legs towards the lower abdomen, with her thighs spread apart. Her arms are placed under her knees and tied together with a band that is suitable.
Therefore, the midwife sits on the right side, and uses the instrument by which she opens the cervix of the uterus, the image of which will be shown later. If you wish to use this instrument, you should estimate the depth of the woman's uterus so that what enters from the instrument does not exceed the depth of the uterus.

And you hold the instrument, while the servant turns the tube until it opens the cervix of the uterus. If the discharge appears and can be touched by hand and is soft and yielding, you should cut it at its head with a broad forceps. Once all the fluid has been discharged.

Then treat with the ointment suitable for this purpose for two days until it heals.
And the uterus and wound may be washed by injecting them with water and honey, then with boiled water in which the root of the datura or long thorn has been cooked. Then return to the ointment. If the abscess is hidden inside the uterus, it should be treated accordingly.
It is advisable to refrain from treating it with iron. It should be treated as we have mentioned in the division.
The Fifty-Seventh Chapter.
In Teaching the Surgeons How to Treat Living Fetuses That Have Been Delivered Abnormal.
The midwife should first know the normal pattern of birth. One of its signs is that you see the woman laboring downward and longing to breathe fresh air, and her postpartum condition becomes easier for her.
And to hasten the baby's delivery, know that this birth is on the natural pattern and its exit is with its head and the placenta either with it or hanging from its neck. If you see these signs, it should be pressed on her abdomen so that the baby comes out quickly.
For if it descends with its head, the placenta descends with it and should be cleaned properly. Any birth other than this is unnatural and condemned, as the baby may descend on its feet with its hands coming out before its head and feet.
And if it is one hand or one foot or he comes out with his head and one hand or he comes out folded, or perhaps he turns onto his back, and the like of these condemned shapes, it is advisable for the midwife to be skilled and delicate in all these matters and to beware of errors and mistakes.
I have explained each of them and how to apply the remedy for it so that you may rely on this and understand it, if the fetus comes out headfirst in a natural birth and great difficulty befalls the woman with the delivery and I see her strength has weakened, then I seat her on a chair and order women to attend to her.
She is then fomented with boiled horsemint and wet ointments, then the midwife inserts a small clamp between her fingers and either cuts the placenta with it or cuts it with her nail until the moisture within it flows out, and she squeezes the woman's abdomen until the fetus descends.
If it does not descend, then the woman should be injected with the juice of horsemint mixed with ointment of the rectum. Then, after the injection, you should instruct her to sneeze and blow her nose with a condes (a type of tube or reed). Hold her mouth and nostrils; the fetus will come out from its cavity. If the hands of the fetus come out first, then you should gently return them little by little.
If they do not enter, place the woman on a stool and raise her legs above. Then shake the stool on the ground and the woman should hold herself to prevent falling during the shaking. If the hands do not enter and the fetus has died, cut them off and pull out the rest of the fetus.
Or tie his hands with a cloth and pull them gently; the fetus will come out. If the fetus comes out on its feet, then you should raise its feet and turn the fetus little by little until you straighten it, then take one of its feet and extend it slowly.
If they come out to the thighs, order her to strain and sniff with the condens. If it comes out in this way, then if it does not come out as described above and otherwise, gently return the fetus a little at a time until it is on the natural shape; then it will come out smoothly. If all of the above fails.
Take one part of the mucus of the ox hoove, one part of the mallow mucus, one part of the fat of the sheep's tail, and one part of dissolved gum. Pound all in a mortar well, then insert it into the woman's vagina and below her navel. Then seat her in cold water until it reaches the ovaries.
If you see that it has leaked below her, make her a pessary of mercury and she must bear it. When she holds the pessary for an hour, seat her on a chair, then sniff with her mouth and nose closed and gently squeeze her lower abdomen. The fetus will come out from its position, coming out with its knees and hands first.
If it comes out in this manner, have her slowly insert her hands further. Then, let the woman lie on her back and dangle her legs downward while lying on a bed, and keep her hands together. Gently squeeze above her abdomen a little at a time. Then, remove what is under her feet from the pillows so that she is tilted downward. If the fetus does not come out, take both her legs and move them strongly. Gently squeeze above the ovaries a little at a time until the fetus ascends upward. Then, let the midwife insert her hand and gently adjust the position of the fetus.
And the woman must be delivered until the fetus is born, with the fetus emerging with its back turned and one of its hands hanging down. If she can manage to push it back in, then let the woman remain in that position. If she cannot do so, cause her to sit up and make her walk. If she cannot walk, then have her lie down.
Place her on a bed and shake her thighs vigorously. Then apply the spoon described from the salivas. If she has a miscarriage, seat her in a chair and proceed to manage the return of the hand and the alignment of the fetus in its natural position. Instill medicine into the woman and order her to be delivered until the fetus is born.
The fetus should be born on its feet, with its hands extended and its face towards the back of the mother. The midwife should hold the hand of the fetus, then turn it little by little and align it gently. Once it is aligned, apply what we have described of the ointment and salivas to her breast.
Then make her move slightly. If she does so, seat her on a chair and order her to tilt towards the right side. Then make her be delivered and instill medicine into her nose with a condens. It will cause the fetus to be born standing on its side.
If it descends into the birth canal in this manner with the placenta, cut the placenta with your fingernail until it is free of moisture. If it is attached to the face or neck of the fetus, sever it at the umbilical cord to prevent the fetus from suffocating and dying. Then push the fetus inside until it is in the correct position.
And make the woman be delivered several times, for it comes out easily. The delivery of twins or multiple fetuses. Know that twins are often born, and sometimes three or four may be born and live, though this is rare. As for five, it is something outside the natural order and they never live at all.
And they surround them, even if there are many from one fetus and they separate by a membrane barrier between each of them, fixed in the navel cord of each one. And they may be born as one newborn would be born naturally and easily, or they may be born as we described, disgracefully.
And if some of them experience difficulty at birth and become what we said of the unnatural shapes, adjust them as we described. Let the midwife be gentle and do what she does with gentleness and delay, and adapt to each shape with whatever means are available to her that lead to safety.
What may be conceived in the womb are fetuses that may be one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, and more than ten. It has been reported to me that a woman gave birth to seven, and another to fifteen all of them formed.
By the estimation of the Most Merciful, All-Knowing, all this should be within the knowledge of the midwife, for it is possible that she may encounter such cases someday, and she should handle them as they require.
The Sixty-Seventh Chapter.
In the Extraction of the Dead Fetus.
If you treat the dead fetus as described in the division of treatment and it does not come out, and you are forced to use your hand, you should examine whether the woman is strong and free from symptoms that one fears might be harmed. If so, the woman should lie on a bed on her back.
And her head should be tilted downwards, and her legs raised. A servant should hold her on both sides or tie her to the bed to prevent her body from being pulled when the fetus is extended.
Then the mouth of its womb is moistened with wet fingers along with the saliva of the camel and acacia, and the sesame seed. Then the midwife anoints her hand with these substances. She then enters it into the womb gently, seeking a place to insert the forceps of the fetus, and the appropriate positions accordingly.
Look, if the fetus is presenting so that it can be delivered by forceps on its head, then insert the forceps into its eyes or its forehead or its mouth or its neck or under its chin or under its clavicles or in the nearby positions of the ribs or under the armpits.
And if it is to be delivered by its feet, then do so at the perineum and the middle ribs. It is best to hold the forceps with the right hand and direct them between the fingers of the left hand. Enter the hand gently and insert the forceps into one of those positions we have mentioned.
Until you reach something empty, then insert another forceps or a third one if needed to make the traction equal and not tilt towards any side. Then extend it evenly, but do not let the extension be only straight; move it in every direction.
It should be easy for it to come out, as is done with a tooth when extracting it. It is necessary between these steps that the extension be relaxed. If it gets stuck on any side, then the midwife should anoint some fingers with oil and insert them from that side to turn what got stuck. If part of the fetus comes out, then move the forceps to other positions.
Raise it slightly. Do this until the fetus comes out completely. If a hand comes out first and cannot be pushed back due to compression, then wrap it with a cloth and pull it until it comes out completely, then cut it.
Either in the wrist or in the elbow, thus it should be done in the other hand and in the legs, if the head of the fetus is large and there is pressure on it during birth or if there is water collected in its head, you should introduce a spinal-like probe between the fingers.

If the chest gets compressed then, if the chest does not decompress and it cannot be delivered, cut it open as much as you can. If it is low in the abdomen or has a swelling, you should incise it to allow the moisture to drain out.
If the fetus is in a breech position, then pulling it is easy and adjusting it to the birth canal is simple. If it gets compressed at the abdomen or chest, you should pull it with a cloth wrapped around your hand and split the abdomen or chest until the contents within drain out.
If all the other organs are extracted and only the head remains, and it has turned back, the midwife should use her left hand. If the birth canal is open, she should insert her hand into the cervical opening and reach for the head with it, pulling it with her fingers into the birth canal. Then she should insert forceps or two forceps and pull the head with them.
If the mouth of the womb has united with a hot tumor, it is not necessary to apply pressure on it; rather, it should be treated by applying wet and fatty substances, using compresses, and sitting in waters that relax and moisturize.
And if the fetus is on its side, if it can be turned, then what we have mentioned for a living fetus should be applied. If this cannot be done, then it should be cut and removed. It must not leave anything of the placenta inside at all. When you finish your treatment, apply what we have mentioned for the treatment of hot tumors that occur in the womb.
If there is a bleeding, she should immerse in contracting waters and apply all other treatments. I have seen a woman who became pregnant and the fetus died in her womb, then she became pregnant again.
Then the other fetus also died. It occurred to her after a long time as a tumor in her genital area, which swelled until it opened and began to discharge pus. She was called upon for treatment, and I treated her for a long time. The wound did not heal, so I applied some of the strong suction ointments.
Then a bone came out from the place, and after days another bone came out. I was amazed at this, for the abdomen is not a place that has bones; I supposed it to be from the bones of the dead fetus. So I examined the wound and found many bones, including those from the head of the fetus.
I continued to follow this until I extracted many bones, and the woman was in her best condition. She lived like this for some time, exuding only a slight amount of pus from the place. I have mentioned here only this rarity.

The Ninety-seventh Chapter.
In the Treatment of the Perineum Not Pierced.
Many boys are born with their perineum not pierced, which may be blocked by a thin film. The midwife should puncture this film with her finger; otherwise, she should incise it with a sharp forceps. She must be careful not to touch the muscle.
Then she places on it a cloth soaked in the drink and oil, and then treats it with ointments until it heals. If you fear that it may become blocked, insert a lead tube into the opening for several days, and remove it when the child passes feces.
And the perineum may also become blocked due to the healing of a wound or a tumor. It should be incised where the wound has healed, and then treated as we have mentioned for other cases and with lead strips.
The Eightieth Chapter.
In the Treatment of Nawsir Occurring Below.
The nawsir occurring below is a complication characterized by hardness and constriction that happens near the perineum from outside or within one of the sides. The nawsir can be one or more.
If the complication delays, it will open and discharge a white watery exudate or a thin pus. Some of these may extend to the probe and the intestine, while others may not. The ones that do extend can be identified by what comes out from them in terms of feces and gas when using the purgative enema.
Perhaps worms may come out of it, and some of these passages may extend to the bladder and the urethra. Some may extend to the knee joint and the heel. The passage that extends to the perineum can also be identified by its extension, while the non-extended ones cannot.
That you insert your third finger into the perineum and introduce a thin probe of copper or iron into the passage. If there is curvature in the passage, then introduce a thin probe of tin or a hair from a horse's tail.
Until you feel the probe or the hair in your finger. If you do not feel it at all, and nothing comes out from the hole in terms of feces, gas, or worms as we have said, then know that it is not extended, and act promptly with treatment.
If the passage extends to the bladder or the urethra, its indication is the discharge of urine from it and its inability to adhere to the area when treated with medications. If it extends to the knee joint or the heel, its indication is the arrival of the probe there.
If there is no curvature to the bone and pain in a certain area, and thin pus continually discharges from it, and no treatment works on it and it does not adhere to ointment, then none of these extended passages will ever heal.
Treatment is in vain for those affected by it among the ignorant physicians. As for that which is not dangerous and not chronic, one hopes for its cure with iron as I have described and what I have tried, and it is that the patient be laid on his back before you.
He extends his legs upward and bends his thighs toward his belly. Then you introduce a copper or lead probe into the curvature until you know where the probe ends. If the patient feels it near the anus, you should introduce your third finger into the anus.
If you feel the probe in your finger has passed through by itself, uncovered with no sensation of a membrane or flesh between your finger and it, then know for certain that it is dangerous. Do not waste effort on it, as there is no cure for it as we have said.
They have said that it may cure in some people rarely. One of the treatments that one hopes will be beneficial is to heat a thin iron plate according to the size of the curvature as previously mentioned, and then introduce it hot into the curvature until it reaches near the anus, then reinsert it two or three times.
Until you know that it has burned all the excessive necrotic flesh that resembles a bird's quill. Then treat it with a moistened sponge in oil until the burned flesh is removed, then treat it with ointments until it heals.
Otherwise, it will not be cured by anything other than this treatment. As for when you introduce the probe and it does not pass to your finger in the anus, and there is a thick barrier of flesh or membrane between it and the probe, and you see the curvature as the surface of the skin, then at that time cut the skin from the beginning of the curvature. And as you pass the incision with the probe in the nostril until you reach with the incision where the end of the probe has reached and the probe discharges and falls out, then you cleanse those congealed meats that resemble bird feather tubes and nothing remains of them.
Then treat it with ointments of healing until it heals. And cut the blood and evaporate the moisture, then treat it with ointment-soaked wool in oil or powdered sulfur in oil until the wound discharges and those burned meats come out in the discharge. Then treat the wound subsequently with healing ointments that break up hard flesh.
And they are the medicines that have a constricting and drying effect; for if it constricts, then it has healed and there will be no recurrence. If the nostril has reached the depth of the nasal cavity but is far from the surface of the body, insert your finger into the nasal cavity and probe with it.

The eighty-first section.
On the treatment of hemorrhoids that bleed and their excision and the healing of the incision.
Hemorrhoids are of two kinds. Either they are inside the rectum, resembling the lips of a woman or like grapes, some small and some large, and blood always flows from them.
And they can be single or multiple. They can also be external, near the edges of the rectum. However, these external hemorrhoids are generally less moist; yellow water or little blood slowly flows from them continuously and they appear to match the color of the body.
The treatment for hemorrhoids inside the rectum is to advise the patient to purge and cleanse until the rectum expels its contents, revealing the hemorrhoids. You should then tie them with forceps or grasp them with your fingernail, and cut them off at their base. If the forceps do not hold due to their moisture and laxity.
Tie it with a rough cloth or a piece of iron wire, or grasp it with your fingers, then cut it off. After cutting, sprinkle some sharp charcoal pieces on it to serve as an alternative to cauterization, or burn it as described in the section on cauterization.
Then treat it with other treatments until it heals. If the rectum does not expel its contents, administer a purge to the patient containing a little laxative to cleanse what is in the rectum and facilitate its quick expulsion when the patient cleanses. Squeeze out the hemorrhoids that have come out of the rectum gently and easily.
And take it with your nail or suspend it with forceps and cut it then treat it as we mentioned until it heals. And if one dislikes cutting with iron, it is advisable to use pincers in this manner: take a wound thread and insert it into a needle.
Then draw the cyst upwards and puncture it with the needle from its base on the other side. Wrap the ends of the thread around the needle, which is crossed over the cyst, and pull the cyst tightly. Tighten the thread and remove the needle. Do this for all cysts, leaving one unharmed.
To expel its bloody contents, then place a cloth soaked in rose or cucumber oil on the cyst and put it over the cyst. Order the patient to remain still, then leave him until the cysts fall off. If they fall off, treat them with ointments and other remedies until they heal.
As for the treatment of scarring, it often occurs from dryness and the grip of the nature. If it lingers and no remedy works, it is advisable to excise it with forceps or your nail until it becomes moist and the upper crust that prevents its healing is removed.
Then treat it until it heals as much as it should. If it does not heal, redress it with a more severe excision until it heals properly and sloughs off. Then treat it, for it will heal.
The Second and Eighty-First Chapter.
On the Treatment of Bent and Straight Pins, Hard Cysts, and Wart.
The nail is a round knot in the color of the body, resembling the head of a nail, found throughout the body but especially in the soles of the feet and fingers. Pain from it often occurs during walking.
It is necessary to cut around the nail and extract it with a scalpel or forceps, then remove it from its root. If you wish, treat it as mentioned in the relevant section for that. As for the hard wart, each one is a small rough hardened round growth on the surface of the body.
It often occurs in the hands of boys. Its treatment is to expand the wart and cut it or rub it with a silk thread or hair until it falls off. If you wish, treat it as mentioned with fire or with sharp medicine.
Warts, whether inverted or not, can be removed with the instrument described in the treatment for the ant. As for the ant, it is also a small rough hardened growth that penetrates deeply into the body's surface; if it is affected by cold, one feels something similar to an ant bite within it.
It can occur throughout the body, but is more common in the hands. Its treatment is to take a tube from an ostrich feather or a strong eagle feather and make that tube surround the ant until the circle of the tube encompasses it from all sides. Then, turn your hand with the tube until you cut around the ant.
It can penetrate deep into the flesh, and the ant will be removed from its root. If you prefer, you can use a copper or iron tube in this manner.
The upper tube to the tendons is stiffened and folded for ease of finger control and manipulation, and if you prefer, seal the needle as mentioned earlier for blister treatment in the section on blistering.
The Third and Eighth Chapter.
In the images of the instruments used for injection in cases of dysuria, diarrhea, and smallpox.
It can be made of silver or copper or brass, either drawn or beaten. These instruments can be made in small and large sizes according to the users. It should be made small for use in treating young boys whose urethras are narrow or stricture-prone. The syringe should be very delicate. Image of a large syringe:.
The top stopcock through which the fluid is drawn should be wide in this manner, with a stop to attach the fluid as you see. Its lower end, which enters the urethra, should be stiff and very smooth towards the tendons. On one side, there are two holes, and on the other side, one hole.
The hole should be of the size of a thumb's breadth or slightly larger. The tube through which you place the medicine, made from the bladder of an animal or the skin of a sheep, should be crafted in the shape of a small spoon.
It should have many holes, spaced as much as the width of a finger apart. Then, a thin thread made from doubled woolen threads, about ten strands or similar, is inserted into these holes, and the fluid is drawn in like a spoon. If the medicine is placed therein, tighten at the head of the injected between the stones tightly, then inject it, and this is a figure of the circle of the ziqq and the hole.
The method of administering it is to fill the bladder with the medicine, heated to a temperature that can be tolerated by the patient, and beware that it should not be too hot or too cold. Then, lie the patient on his back and elevate his legs above his head.
It is placed under him a mat or a blanket. Then, the tip of the cannula is smeared with ointment or egg white or dodder sap or similar substances. Then it is inserted into the cavity gently. The patient then holds the ziqq (a type of cannula) with both hands and presses it tightly until all that is in the cannula is discharged into the intestines.
Then, the cannula is removed and the patient is made to elevate his legs against the wall. If the medicine stimulates him to defecate, he should strain as much as he can. If he sleeps through the night, it is more effective for the condition. If the cannula is used for cases of diarrhea and he needs to expedite the discharge, the procedure should be repeated until he recovers.
If there are hemorrhoids or painful tumors in the cavity, the cannula should be very smooth and gentle, different from those used for boys. This is a figure of a gentle cannula with its skin tightly stretched on it.
Chapter Forty-Eight.
In the Treatment of Wounds.
I have already discussed the division of treatment similar to cauterization, and here I will treat the application by hand and with medicines as perfectly as possible. I say that wounds differ according to the thing causing the wound and according to the place where it occurs.
The things in which surgeries are found are many, such as a stone strike or a sword cut or a knife wound or a spear thrust or a rod or an arrow and the like from many things.
And as for the surgeries according to the places of the body, they are such as the wound that occurs on the head or the neck or the chest or the abdomen or the liver and the like from the organs.
And I am describing the treatment of some surgeries to make it a measure and a rule for all other surgeries. I begin with simple head injuries especially, because the compound ones will be mentioned at the beginning of the third chapter of this book.
And I say that if a simple wound occurs on the head and there is no bone fracture, look whether it was caused by a stone or something similar, and whether it only pierced the skin and the wound is large, and fearing the occurrence of a hot swelling in the patient, treat it promptly and apply cold compresses at the site. And do not delay this. Let him bleed from the wound according to his strength if there is no obstruction to bleeding. This is especially true if the blood coming from the wound is small. The bleeding should be from the opposite side of the wounded area.
And warn the patient against filling up, drinking thick liquids, and eating heavy foods. If something prevents bleeding, reduce food intake and avoid meat and strong drinks. Apply a cloth soaked in rose oil alone or with a drink that has contracting properties to the wound if it develops a hot swelling.
And if you are concerned about the hot swelling, apply his blood to the wound if it is fresh and has not been changed by the respiratory air, which I will describe to you shortly. If the air has already changed it, apply some ointments to it.
Until the pus matures, then treat it until it heals. If the wound is large and is from a sword cut or similar and its edges did not come together with the vessels, suture it as I have described in suturing abdominal wounds.
If the skin has revealed the bone and is hanging loose, with its hold being only by a slight ligament, cut it off then treat the wound with medicines that will cause solid flesh to grow in its place of the skin. Order the patient to nourish himself with foods that are strengthening, such as meats and lentils and the like.
If corruption occurs in the skin and it does not adhere to the bone, cut out all the corrupted tissue, throw it away, then treat the wound. If there is a vein or artery in these wounds that bleeds but the bleeding does not stop with medicines, examine the vessel.
If it did not necrose, amputate it with the forceps and ligate it. If necessity demands and what we have mentioned does not help, cauterize it until the bleeding stops. If these wounds are small and shallow, treat them easily and gently, sufficient treatment being to sprinkle them with this salve while they are still bleeding.
Before the air changes it, a prescription of salve is: take of frankincense one part, and of myrrh two parts, and of ashes of lime or unquenched lime three parts. Crush all of them, sift them, and apply them to the wound and tie it tightly so that it adheres well.
It congeals with the blood, then tie it from above with the vessels and leave it alone without loosening it as long as it does not swell; for the medicine will not come off until it heals. The ash may do this by itself if frankincense and myrrh are not available.
And this may also be done with a tube in many large operations if he masters its placement upon it and tightens it, and the operation is soft by its blood without changing until the air changes it somewhat, especially if it is in the time of summer.
And there is no active meaning in placing this tube. It may be filled with some mature ointments or with a porridge made from barley flour mixed with water and honey until the pus exudes, then it should be treated with other treatments until it heals.
And if there is a fracture of the bone with the wound and it is slight,牵引牵引之，用夹板固定，关于头部骨折的治疗已在颈部手术中提及。若伤口发生在颈部，则其治疗与轻微的头部伤口并无区别。
And if it cuts a nerve or a vein in the neck, and if it is a nerve, there is no remedy other than to avoid treating it with anything that constricts severely, such as zanjir, zağ, and similar substances, because they harm the nerve and spasm it.
And nothing cold should be applied to the wound at all, because the essence of the nerve is cold. Its connection with the brain, which is the most noble of organs, should be avoided. What you treat it with should be gentle medicines such as a wet napkin soaked in fresh water, or oiled with rose or tangerine oil.
If it is also washed with fresh water and other metallic stones in this manner, and ointments, then if the wound is large use stitching or suture its lips with ligatures, then treat it until it heals.
If the wound is deep and contains a concealed collection at its bottom where pus has accumulated, incise it in the lowest part thereof. If a vessel has been severed within the wound and its blood is still flowing, amputate it or tie it off, or cauterize it if necessity demands so.
If the wound has cut some or all of the pharyngeal sinuses and the ears are intact, suture the skin lips over the pharynx tube without touching the pharynx itself, but smooth and replace it to its natural shape, then tighten it firmly and leave it for days.
Then treat it with ointments that cause contraction and drying until it heals. If the wound has affected the bone, fracture it. If there are bone fragments in it, extract all of them or as many as possible. If you cannot extract them, leave it until the wound suppures and heals, making its extraction easier.
If the wound is raw, sprinkle it with the decorticating powder as described. If it suppurates in the wound and becomes a sinew, treat it with what will be mentioned in its section, in Surgery of the Chest and Between the Shoulders.
If it is a thrust from a spear or sword and you see that it is deep, examine it. If air comes out when the injured person breathes, know that it is a fighting wound. If it is not deep but raw with blood, do not apply any decorticating powder at first, lest the blood be obstructed in its depth.
If it reaches the heart, it will kill the injured person. But apply a attractive ointment to it and let him apply it twice a day during the daytime. If you have no ointment, place a soft cloth in the wound to absorb what comes out of it, and keep the injured person with his head lowered over the wound.
Let it heal if it meets the condition, even though three days or more have passed since the wound, and there is no convulsion nor severe fainting nor oppression in the chest, and I have seen all his conditions suitable. Know then that the wound is healed, treat it with suturing and other treatments until he recovers.
If vision is impaired and the swelling continues unabated, know that it has become a carbuncle. Treat it accordingly; for the ulcers of such wounds let them heal by suturing, even if three days or more have passed since the wound on the chest or back, treat it with the previously mentioned suturing methods.
If it is large or in the glands if it is small, if it has affected the bone and broken off fragments from it, examine the wound and act promptly to remove those fragments if they are clean. If they are not clean, leave them until they become so.
It corrupts the wound, making it easier to remove. As for other recent wounds in other organs, their treatment follows what we have mentioned.
The Fifth and Eighty-First Chapter.
On Wounds of the Abdomen and Protrusion of Intestines and Their Suturing.
The tear in the abdomen may be large or small and medium. The large tear may protrude intestines or several intestines, making their insertion and suturing harder and more difficult.
The small tear, too, may be harder in another respect; hence, its repositioning is more difficult. The intestines, if not inserted into their proper place soon after protrusion, will swell and become harder to insert. Therefore, the medium-sized tear has become the best among tears because it does not make the repositioning of the intestines as difficult as in these two types.
Know that the stitching of the abdomen is upon four aspects. The two common stitches are suitable for stitching the abdomen and other body surgeries. The other two specialized stitches apply to all surgeries, although they are more particularly suited for stitching the abdomen.
And as I describe them to you one by one with explanation and clarification, I say that if the wound is small and something from the intestine has come out and it is difficult to return it, then this is for one of two reasons: either because the tear is small, as we said, or because the intestine was inflated before its return due to air pressure.
And if this is the case, it should be warmed by soaking a wet sponge or cloth in tepid water alone, or in water boiled with Decumbens and Saffron and Belladonna. Then it should be applied to the intestine until the inflation subsides.
And the drink that has griping herbs in it is better than water alone for resolving the inflation. If you see that the inflation has subsided, then moisten the intestine with water boiled with Cinnamon or Baker's Fennel, as it facilitates its entry more easily.
And if return of the intestine is still impossible after this treatment, a small incision should be made in the tear with the instrument used for piercing steel. The first method, if successful, is preferable to the incision. One is forced to make the incision only as a last resort when all other methods have failed. This is the form of the instrument:
Its one end is bent and limited, while the other end is unlimited. The thin end is not as fine as the forceps, but slightly broader. It resembles a small awl, as you can see. If the wound enlarges and the intestine enters, it should be returned to its natural shape.
And its specific place, if you can manage it, is best. As for when the wound is large and is in the lower part of the abdomen, the patient should lie on his back with his legs elevated above his head. And when it is in the upper part of the abdomen, he should have his head and chest elevated above his feet.
And likewise, if the wound is in one of the sides of the abdomen, make your aim and purpose to have the side with the surgery elevated above the other side. Thus, this should be applied in great surgeries as well as in medium-sized ones.
As for small surgeries, place him as you are able to. Then, have before you a kind attendant who holds the entire wound with both hands, brings together its lips, then reveals a bit at a time to the one performing the suturing.
This is the characteristic of a common suture: you take one needle or several needles according to the size of the wound. Then, leave a finger's breadth from one edge of the wound and insert one needle without putting any thread into the edges of the skin. With the edges of the flaps beneath the skin from within, you pass them from that side. Then, you gather both edges of the skin and both edges of the flap, making four loops. Next, you tighten a doubled thread around the needle several times from both sides until the edges of the wound meet tightly.
Then, leave a finger's breadth and insert another needle. Tighten it with the thread as you did with the first needle. Continue doing this with the needles as needed until you complete suturing the entire wound. Let the needles be of medium thickness between the thick and the thin.
Because very thin needles cut the flesh quickly and easily, and similarly, they are difficult to enter the skin near tough areas, therefore, it should be medium in softness and hardness, and the needle should not be inserted close to the edge of the skin.
To prevent the flesh from cutting quickly and the wound from opening before healing, and to ensure that the suturing is not too far apart so as not to hinder the wound's healing, then cut the ends of the needles to avoid injuring the patient when asleep, and provide it with ties from torn linen cloth on all sides to hold the needle ends.
And leave it until you know that the wound has healed. This type of suturing with needles is most appropriate for small surgeries, as it may suffice with one or two needles or similar.
Or as for the method of suturing for the second general case, it is to gather the four edges with one stitch, meaning the edges of the skin and the edges of the membrane, using a needle with a folded thread of medium softness and hardness. Then, when these four edges are sewn with this needle, withdraw the needle from the same side where you started.
Let the thread be tied from above the wound, so that the suturing is done according to the method of tying goods with a knot. Make sure there is some thickness of the small finger between each stitch and this type of suturing is known by all people.
And with this suturing, a wound was treated in a man's belly who had been cut by a knife, and the size of the surgical tear was more than an inch. Two inches of the middle intestine had come out, and the tear was in the center of the belly.
He repeated it after the intestines remained outside the wound for twenty-four hours. The wound healed in about fifteen days, and he treated it until it痊愈，之后又活了很多年，能够应对各种状况。医生们断定他绝不会再痊愈了。
And it is wonderful that I did not treat him with a ointment, for I was in a place where there was nothing of the medicines. So I would place a wet cotton on the wound twice a day and take care to wash it with honey water until it healed.
And as for one of the two types of specialized suturing, I will mention it in the words of Galen: Begin with suturing the skin and insert the needle from outside to inside. Once you have passed the needle through the skin and the muscle going straight along the length of the abdomen.
I left the edge of the membrane on the side where I inserted the needle and passed the needle through its other edge from inside to outside in the other margin of the membrane. Once I have done this, I passed it again through the same margin of the membrane from outside to inside.
And leave the edge of the membrane on this side, pass the needle through its other edge from inside to outside, and as you pass it through the membrane, also pass it to the edge of the muscle on that side, until you pass all of them.
Then begin also from this side and suture it with the edge of the membrane on the other side. Remove the needle from the skin near it, then push it back into that skin and suture the edge of the membrane on the other side with this edge of the muscle.
And remove it from the skin on that side, and do that again and do it time after time until you sew the entire surgery according to that example. And in brief, this manner of sewing is like the sewing of the falconers for the falcon.
And sew the septum from one side with the skin edge and leave it open on the other side until you finish, as for the second type of special sewing mentioned by Galen, this is exactly what he said.
And sew it according to the example that some physicians sew it, by bringing each part together with its counterpart naturally, joining the edge of the septum to its other edge and the edge of the margin to its other edge, as I describe to you.
You should stitch the margin of the margin close to you from outside, penetrating it only and leaving the septal margins. Then withdraw the needle and reinsert it from outside to inside in both septal margins, withdrawing it also.
And pass it from inside to outside in the other margin of the margin on the opposite side. This type of sewing is better than the easy general sewing that you have been shown. This is exactly what Galen said. Some have also said that the abdominal stitching can be done with two needles. And do this by inserting one thread into both and starting by inserting the needle from your side, passing it to the other side. Insert the other needle from the opposite side and pass it back from your side according to the manner of masons' sewing.
Know that if the wound is in the middle of the abdomen, suturing it is harder than at other places in the abdomen. As for the treatment of the injury, its rule in curing is like that of all injuries; namely, if you encounter the wound fresh with its blood before the air changes it, and return the intestines and suture and secure it, apply upon it the heated irons.
If the wound has been changed by the air, apply some ointments that you prepare until it suppurates and the sutures drop out and the edges unite. Then treat it as you treat other wounds until it heals.
If you do not have medicines, apply to it old cotton when it begins to suppurate and change it twice a day as I have taught you until it heals. For in most cases you will not need another treatment if the wounds are simple. If you fear that the wound might involve the main organs in pain, treat it accordingly.
It is necessary to soak a soft cotton in moderately heated oil or in rose fat and place it around the areas between the navel and the hips. If he feels pain or corruption within, often this is the case; so inject him with a diluted astringent drink.
And especially if the corruption has reached the intestines and become an open wound penetrating its cavity. Know that what is thick among the intestines is easier to heal, and what is thin among them is harder to heal.
As for the intestine known as the "fasting bowel," it does not accept healing from a wound that occurs in it at all. This is because it contains many large veins, and its inner lining is thin and close to the nature of nerves. As for if the pus from the wound protruded and you encountered it fresh, return it according to your usual method of returning the bowel.
If it persists for a time and turns green or black, it should be tied above the place that turned black to prevent bleeding, for there are veins and arteries in the swelling. Then cut what is below that bandage.
And make the ends of the thread attached from below the surgery outside of it to make it easier for you to pull and remove when the swelling and wound discharge occur. This refers to the wound that appears in the intestine; if a tear appears in the intestine and is small.
For it may heal in some people, as I have seen a man who was stabbed in his abdomen by an arrow; the wound was on the right side of the stomach. The wound healed and became a fistula from which feces and gas would exit. I treated him without hoping for a cure. I continued to treat him until he recovered and the wound healed. Seeing the wound had healed, I feared that something harmful might occur within him, but indeed, he was never afflicted by any such harm and remained in his best condition. He recovered, eating and drinking normally, engaging in sexual activity, using the bath, and being well attended to. Some practitioners have noted that when a wound appears in the intestine and is small, it should be sutured in this manner.
It should be taken thus: The heads of large ants are first extracted, then the edges of the wound are gathered, and an ant is placed there with its mouth open over the wound's edges. When it grabs and tightens its mouth, cut off its head; for it adheres and does not come loose. Then place another ant near the first one.
And continue to do so with many ants in proportion to the wound, then replace them and suture the wound; for those heads will remain stuck in the intestines until they cause it to swell and the patient recovers. No harm will come to the affected person at all, and the intestines can also be sutured with fine thread.
He who excises from the two canals the sticky substance adhering to the animal after it enters a needle, should take the end of this thread from the canals and excise some tissue. Then he should tie at its end a thin folded cotton thread, and then insert that thread into the needle. And there is a thread from the canals which is used to suture the intestines, then it is replaced into the body. This method of suturing with ants and canals is based on hope and expectation.
And if the wound is large and wide, especially if it is in one of the delicate intestines, there is no remedy for it at all, and it will not recover at all.
The Sixth and Eighth Chapter.
In the Treatment of Common Cold and Nasal Discharge.
Know that every wound or tumor, if it lingers and becomes old and turns into a chronic ulcer without healing and continues to discharge pus, is called a nasour in general for any body part. We call it a common cold, and the nasour.
It is in reality a stiff, white concretion without pain, having a cavity like the cavity of a bird's feather.
And for this reason, some have called it a feather. At times, it becomes wet and continues to discharge pus constantly; at other times, the wetness may cease. The wetness can be abundant or scanty, thick or thin.
And I have mentioned in the division when describing wounds that every wound which does not heal and in which flesh does not grow, is due to one of nine causes. One of these causes is either a deficiency of blood in the body or its poor quality or because there is within it and on its edges solid flesh that prevents the growth of good flesh. And either because it is full of pain and filthiness, or because the wound itself is putrid and the material that nourishes it is of poor quality, or because the medicine used to treat it is not appropriate, or because there has been a deterioration in the locality due to the nature of the epidemic, or because of something specific to the locality.
And either because it is full of pain and filthiness, or because the wound itself is putrid and the material that nourishes it is of poor quality, or because the medicine used to treat it is not appropriate, or because there has been a deterioration in the locality due to the nature of the epidemic, or because of something specific to the locality. As was presented in the city of Sargasso, where it is difficult for diseases to mature and tumors to heal naturally, either because there is one bone or several bones. I have explained all these causes and their symptoms and treatments with medicines in the division.
And here, I must acquaint you with the treatment of fistula and colds that occur through manual intervention. Know that fistulas can occur in all parts of the body; some lead to large veins or arteries, or to nerves.
Or to a sinus, or to an intestine, or to the bladder, or to a rib, or to a vertebra of the spine, or to a joint composed of many parts such as the hand and the foot. Some may lead to a part near a major organ or something similar.
For those fistulas of this nature, they are among the diseases that are difficult to heal and do not respond to treatment or effort. If there are fistulas that do not reach these mentioned locations, then there is hope for their healing.
And in order to come to know this, take a probe of copper or iron if the catheter passes straight. If there is curvature in the catheter, examine it with a thin lead probe because lead softens its body.
It will slide upon entering and bend toward the curvature. If the catheter has many openings, you cannot discern them with the probe. So inject one of its openings with moisture; it will flow towards the other openings and drain.
Then examine it in any way possible to determine if there is a bone or nerve, or if the catheter's depth is far or near, or if it has one catheter with many openings. Stand firm on all this by your full capacity of probing and the pain it causes when you gently touch the area with your hand.
And so with such signs and symptoms of the tumor, when you stand firm on all this as a reality, then proceed to the treatment with confidence, which is to look and see if it is.
The catheter is obvious and close or in a safe place distant from the joint or nerve or blood vessel or vein or any of the places mentioned to you. Cut the catheter as described above and extract from it the congealed matter, rotten flesh, and excess flesh.
And treat what grows in its opening from flesh or excrescence and the like until it heals. If the catheter has a deep base and is straight, you should cut it deeply as much as possible, then cleanse it of all its rotten flesh.
Then use the triple-threaded floss for acute medicines and insert it into the bottom of the canal which you reach with the iron. Do this several times until that sharp medicine eats all that remains in the bottom of the canal from decay.
Then apply ointments that promote healthy flesh growth until it heals. If it does not heal thereby, incise and drain as previously described. If the cause of the canal is bone and you find that satisfactory, then trephine and section it as I have instructed you, provided nothing prevents you from doing so.
If a vein or nerve or primary organ, as we have said, is revealed to you and there is some decay and blackness in it, strip it until the decay disappears. Then treat it with flesh-growing remedies until it heals. If it does not heal and the pus persists as it used to do.
Know that you have not completely removed all the decay. Therefore, expose everything again thoroughly and cleanse and remove it to the best of your ability. Then apply ointments; if it heals, otherwise know that this decay is deep within the decaying tissue, so expose everything again thoroughly.
Examine and cleanse it to the best of your ability. The decayed bone is small and you can extract it using delicate forceps suitable for this purpose.
If there are many bones, examine and extract all of them without leaving anything behind to the best of your ability. If something from the ligaments obstructs you and there is no danger in cutting it, then cut those ligaments and the flesh if present, and free the bones.
If it is not possible for you to extract the bones, apply something to dress the wound and leave it until the flesh and ligaments around those bones putrefy, and take care that the wound does not heal by apposition of the incision you made in your work.
But apply thereon if you fear that to cotton soaked in powdered sulfur with oil or cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment or one of the green ointments; for when it putrefies those ligaments and decays the bones, their extraction and traction will be easy.
If it is a large bone such as the thigh bone or shin bone, and only its surface has rotted, then thoroughly strip it of the decay until the blackness and corruption are gone, then set the wound. If a large part of it has rotted and the corruption has reached the marrow of the bone, it must be removed.
And cut it completely to where the corruption ends. Then treat it until it heals. I inform you of a case that was presented to a man in his thigh, so that it may serve as an example and aid in your treatment. This man was a young adult.
接近三十岁的时候，他出现了腿部疼痛的症状，原因是体内有异物活动直至与腿部相连并肿胀成巨大的肿瘤。病因并非来自外部。时间久了，医生的误诊使病情恶化，最终肿瘤破裂。
A great deal of material discharged from it, and he was poorly treated, until the leg became gangrenous with many openings discharging pus and body moisture. A group of doctors treated him for about two years, but none among them was skilled in surgical techniques.
Until he reached me, I saw his thigh and the pus flowing from those openings in great abundance. The leg had become emaciated and its color had turned yellow. I inserted the探针之一进入其中的一个开口，探针抵达了骨头，然后我彻底检查了所有的开口。
I found them communicating with each other from all sides of the thigh. I incised one of these openings until a part of the bone was revealed, and I found it corrupted, decayed, blackened, and putrefied, until the hole reached the brain, spreading what had been disclosed to me.
And I removed the corrupted bone, as I thought that there was no corruption in the bone other than what I cut and spread and had excised. Then I made use of the adhesive medicines to bind the wound for a longer period, but it did not heal. Later, I returned and revealed the bone again above the first revelation.
I found the corruption connected to the bone. I spread what had been revealed to me also from that corruption. Then I bound it again, but it did not bind or heal. I revealed it once more, and I continued cutting parts of the bone, intending to bind it, but it would not bind until I cut nearly a span from the bone.
I removed it with its brain, then bound it with medicines, and it healed quickly and recovered fully. This repetition in his treatment and incision was necessary due to the weak condition of the patient, his low tolerance, and my fear for his life, as he would frequently experience severe fainting from excessive vomiting at all times. He ultimately recovered completely.
We take from the place of the bone flesh strong and healthy, and its condition is well in its body, and its strength has diminished and it acts on its conditions without any affliction affecting it while walking, if it was a broken bone in a place in the body.
It is necessary to treat it in this manner: you take a bandage and tighten it at the end of the broken bone, and order someone to stretch it upwards. Then you make another bandage from thicker cloth than the first.
Then you bind it to the flesh beneath the bone, stretching its end so that the flesh is drawn downward. You uncover the flesh at the place you want to spread it to prevent the saw from injuring the flesh. You place a board or plank underneath the bone from below,紧贴牢固。
If you do this, the saw will not fail to cut the rotten bone. It is necessary for the spreading to be slightly above the place of decay so that there is no decay within the cavity of the bone, which would not be visible externally, forcing you to spread it again.
If the bone is rotten and not broken, but its parts are connected to each other, and the decay is in the middle or some part of it, you should uncover the flesh from all its sides. Then place the board from below, and spread it from the first side where the decay is located.
When you have finished spreading it, spread it from the other side. Let the spreading be slightly away from the decayed area as we said. If the decay is in a joint, cut the rotten joint itself and spread the bone where it connects from the other side.
If the corruption is in the connection of two joints, there is no remedy but excision. If the corruption is in the hand comb or foot comb, the matter of its cure is exceedingly difficult; yet it should be debrided as much as you can perceive and excised to the extent possible.
By what means it can be corrected if no vein or nerve obstructs you, and know that the saws and chisels for cutting these bones are many according to the position of the bones and their setting and their hardness and tenderness and size and smallness and firmness and looseness.
